# Gods and Religion

<!-- FILE_START: ../World Building/Religion/Divinitys_Beacon_Pantheon.md -->

# Divinity’s Beacon — Pantheon

Divinity’s Beacon welcomes all good‑aligned gods, but daily life in the city orbits a practical “working pantheon”: a few major multiversal powers everyone recognizes, plus local gods/saints that rose from frontier need.

The city is governed (religiously and politically) by the **Concord of Radiant Thrones**: a council of high priests and order‑masters from the largest temples. No single faith rules the Beacon, but the Concord sets city‑wide standards for vows, sanctuary, and what kinds of magic are tolerated.

## 1) Great Temples (widely known gods)

These are the skyline‑temples: big, old, and influential.

- **Pelor, the Dawnfather** — Sun, Healing, Agriculture
- **Tyr, the Justicar** — Justice, Law, Retribution
- **Moradin, the Soul Forger** — Creation, Smithing, Protection
- **Selûne, the Moonmaiden** — Moon, Navigation, Protection, Hope
- **Lathander, the Morninglord** — Renewal, Birth, Creativity

{{note
- Pelor and Lathander are often allied in civic rituals (oaths at dawn, renewal after tragedy).
- Tyr sets the legal tone; Moradin equips the orders; Selûne is the city’s “mercy door” (refuge, repentance, lost travelers).
}}

## 2) The Beacon Triad (local patron gods)

These are the three “homegrown” powers most residents feel are *of the Beacon itself*. Their three primary temples form a ceremonial triangle around the central plaza.

### Aurethiel, Dawnmother of Resolve
- **Domains/themes:** Light, Protection, Courage; moral clarity; standing firm against corruption.
- **Worship focus:** public rites, community resilience, vigilance in hard seasons.
- **Common vow:** “Hold the line. Tell the truth. Do not yield to the easy lie.”

### Varrun Stoneheart, the Hearth‑Father
- **Domains/themes:** Life, Forge, Community; craft as service; shelter that endures.
- **Worship focus:** neighborhood hearthposts, communal kitchens, militia chaplains, work‑blessings.
- **Epithet note (merge):** **Aurelian the Hearth‑Warder** is treated as an **epithet/title of Varrun** used by Wardens and frontier folk (when you need “the hearth that guards” more than “the hearth that comforts”).

### Seralyth, the Veiled Listener
- **Domains/themes:** Knowledge, Peace, Truth; confession; secrets kept in trust; oaths with teeth.
- **Worship focus:** confessionals, oath‑binding, counselors, mediators, record‑keepers.
- **Epithet note (merge):** **Vessara, Lady of the Quiet Oath** is treated as an **inner‑mystery title of Seralyth** (a revered mask/aspect invoked for confidential vows, penance, and pact‑severing rites).

## 3) Local Saints & Civic Cults (widely accepted, smaller temples)

These are influential but don’t outrank the Great Temples or the Triad. They often operate as orders within larger faiths.

### Thalanor, the Guiding Gale
- **Domains/themes:** Travel, Pilgrimage, Freedom; crossroads; messengers; “safe roads.”
- **Role in city:** gate‑shrines, caravan blessings, diplomatic neutrality.
- **Merge note:** **Thalanor Brightquill** is kept as **Saint Brightquill**, a famed prophet‑scribe of Thalanor whose cult focuses on inspired speech, diplomacy, and illuminated texts (Knowledge/Light flavor).

### Kelvaris, Warden of the Northern Stars
- **Domains/themes:** Light, Tempest, Navigation; night watch; long patrols; honest bearings.
- **Role in city:** shrines on rooftops, towers, and city walls; patron of scouts and sky‑watchers.

### Myrraline, the Gentle Reclaimer
- **Domains/themes:** Grave, Nature, Renewal; the lawful end; respectful burial; seasons turning.
- **Role in city:** funerary rites, cemetery gardens, anti‑undeath doctrine.

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote DIVINITY’S BEACON — PANTHEON}}

\page

### Eirathene, the Crystal Bloom
- **Domains/themes:** Healing, Growth, Mercy; restoration after crisis; gentle miracles.
- **Role in city:** garden‑hospitals and sanctuaries.
- **Ritual pairing:** In many Beacon rites, **Eirathene and Myrraline** are invoked together as “Bloom and Reclaimer” (life restored, life released).

### Kordun, the Vigilant Flame
- **Domains/themes:** Courage, Sacrifice, Righteous Battle; the will to act when others hesitate.
- **Status (flexible):** treated as either a **minor local god** *or* an **ascended martyr‑saint** depending on which temple tells the story.
- **Role in city:** patron of hardline orders who push strict restrictions on pacts and demon‑tainted magic.

## 4) How worship works in practice

- **House shrines are normal.** A family might honor Pelor at dawn, Seralyth for an oath, and Varrun for a new roof beam.
- **Orders matter more than labels.** “Cleric of Tyr” in the Beacon might be trained by Tyr’s court *and* initiated into Seralyth’s confessional disciplines.
- **The Concord arbitrates conflicts.** When priests disagree, the Concord decides what’s allowed *inside city walls*.

## 5) City stance on arcane magic, warlocks, and pacts

Divinity’s Beacon is not anti‑wizard by default; it is anti‑**unaccountable power**.

- **Arcane study:** tolerated if registered/answerable and not harming innocents.
- **Pacts (warlocks):** the flashpoint. “Good patron” claims are investigated; secret patrons are treated as a civic risk.
- **Seralyth’s role:** confession, truth‑seeking, and oath‑binding are the city’s preferred tools before punishment.
- **Hardliners vs diplomats:** Kordun/Tyr‑aligned orders push bans; Selûne/Thalanor‑aligned factions push monitored tolerance.

## 6) Quick hooks you can drop later

- A Concord vote is split on whether to recognize Kordun as god or saint (political leverage disguised as theology).
- A Seralyth confessor disappears with an oath‑ledger containing names that would start a holy scandal.
- A “Brightquill” preacher is accused of inspiring rebellion via sermons that are secretly encoded.
- A Myrraline funeral rite fails—someone is preventing a soul from “reclaiming,” and the city panics about undeath.
- A Varrun hearthpost is burned; the neighborhood believes it’s a declaration of war.
- An embassy from Solace Nexus arrives asking for sanctuary for a mage accused of pact‑work.


{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote DIVINITY’S BEACON — PANTHEON}}

\page

<!-- FILE_START: ../World Building/Religion/Religious_Practices.md -->
# Religious Practices in Aevoria
*How Faith Works in Daily Life*

Religion in Aevoria is not merely a matter of belief—it shapes daily life, influences commerce, provides social services, and offers tangible benefits through divine magic. This guide explains how worship functions in practice and how your character interacts with the religious institutions of the world.

*For information about specific deities and their mythology, see the Gods and Religion chapter. This guide focuses on practical matters: temple services, costs, holidays, and how faith affects gameplay.*

---

## How Worship Works

### Daily Devotions

Most faithful people in Aevoria maintain simple daily practices:

**Morning Prayers** (5-10 minutes)
- Brief prayer at dawn or upon waking
- Often includes a small offering (incense, food, water)
- May be done at home altar or temple

**Evening Reflections** (5-10 minutes)
- Gratitude for the day's blessings
- Requests for protection through the night
- Common time for family prayers

**Before Meals**
- Brief thanks for sustenance
- Particularly common among farming communities

**Regular Attendance**
- Weekly temple services (common but not universal)
- Monthly festivals (attendance varies by deity and region)
- Major holidays (most people observe these)

### Cleric and Paladin Characters

If your character is a divine spellcaster, your relationship with faith is deeper:

**Daily Preparation**
- You must spend time in prayer to prepare spells (typically 1 hour at dawn)
- This is when you commune with your deity and regain spell slots
- Failing to pray has mechanical consequences (no spell slots)

**Sacred Oaths and Codes**
- Paladins are bound by specific oaths; breaking them has severe consequences
- Clerics maintain alignment and domain restrictions
- Both must strive to further their deity's goals

**Temple Relationships**
- You're expected to visit temples of your deity when possible
- May be called upon to perform services (healing, ceremonies)
- Have access to temple resources and assistance

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote RELIGIOUS PRACTICES IN AEVORIA}}

\page

## Temple Services and Costs

Temples throughout Aevoria provide various services to the faithful and general public. While healing and divine magic aren't cheap, temples operate on sliding scales to serve communities.

### Healing Services

| Service | Typical Cost | Notes |
|---------|--------------|-------|
| **Cure Wounds** (1st level) | 50 gp | Most common healing service |
| **Lesser Restoration** | 80 gp | Disease, poison, paralysis, blindness |
| **Prayer of Healing** (multiple people) | 40 gp per person | Group healing (8 hours) |
| **Greater Restoration** | 200 gp + 100 gp diamond | Serious conditions |
| **Raise Dead** | 1,000 gp + 500 gp diamond | Rarely available; not all temples can provide |
| **Remove Curse** | 100 gp | Varies by curse complexity |
| **Neutralize Poison** | 60 gp | Immediate treatment |

**Donation-Based Alternatives**
Most temples operate on a "pay what you can" model:
- **Suggested donations:** As listed above
- **Poor/Destitute:** Services provided for free or token amounts
- **Wealthy patrons:** Expected to donate generously (2-3× standard cost)

**Why Costs Matter**
Divine magic requires components, temple upkeep, and the time of trained clerics. Temples balance community service with practical needs.

### Ceremonial Services

| Service | Typical Cost | Notes |
|---------|--------------|-------|
| **Blessing** (Bless spell) | 25 gp | Pre-adventure blessing (1 hour) |
| **Consecration** (Ceremony) | 50 gp | Marriage, coming-of-age, etc. |
| **Funeral Rites** | 10-50 gp | Varies by faith and region |
| **Divination** (Augury) | 50 gp | Simple yes/no guidance |
| **Divination** (Divination) | 150 gp | Complex question; rare |
| **Gentle Repose** | 30 gp | Preserves body for 10 days |
| **Atonement** (Atonement) | Varies | Penance for wrongdoing |

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote RELIGIOUS PRACTICES IN AEVORIA}}

\page

### Temple Accommodations

Many temples offer lodging and sanctuary:

| Service | Cost | Notes |
|---------|------|-------|
| **Sanctuary** (safe haven) | Free | Temporary refuge from danger |
| **Simple Lodging** | 5 sp/night | Basic room, communal meals |
| **Private Room** | 1 gp/night | Better accommodations |
| **Long-Term Stay** | Negotiable | Requires service or donation |

**Sanctuary Rules**
Temples provide refuge to those fleeing danger, with conditions:
- Cannot be used to evade justice for serious crimes
- Must respect temple rules (no violence, theft, etc.)
- Limited duration (typically 3-7 days)
- Expects gratitude in form of service or donation

### Information and Guidance

Temples serve as community centers and information hubs:

**Free Services:**
- General spiritual counsel
- Basic information about religious matters
- Community news and gossip
- Referrals to other services

**Paid Services:**
- Research in temple libraries (5-10 gp/day)
- Translation of religious texts (varies)
- Expertise on religious artifacts (varies)

### Regional Variations

**Divinity's Beacon (Holy City)**
- Lower costs (subsidized by pilgrims and wealthy donors)
- More services available
- Highest standards for clerics

**Frontier Settlements (Northreach, Far North)**
- Higher costs (fewer clerics, greater need)
- Limited availability of high-level spells
- May barter goods/services instead of coin

**Vharoxis**
- No temples in traditional sense
- Independent hedge priests charge premium rates
- Quality varies wildly

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote RELIGIOUS PRACTICES IN AEVORIA}}

\page

## Religious Holidays and Festivals

Aevoria's calendar is marked by religious observances. Most people participate in festivals regardless of personal devotion—they're community events as much as religious ones.

### Major Holidays (Observed by Most Faiths)

**The Long Night** (Winter Solstice)
- **When:** Darkest night of the year
- **Observance:** Vigils, lighting of ceremonial fires, stories of endurance
- **Practical Impact:** Most businesses closed; temples provide communal meals
- **Adventuring:** Good time to gather information, as people are talkative and reflective

**The First Thaw** (Early Spring)
- **When:** First true thaw after winter
- **Observance:** Renewal ceremonies, planting blessings, cleaning rituals
- **Practical Impact:** Markets bustle with activity; travel routes reopen
- **Adventuring:** Many contracts and opportunities emerge as people venture out

**Harvest Moon** (Autumn Equinox)
- **When:** Night of the harvest moon
- **Observance:** Feasting, gratitude ceremonies, storing for winter
- **Practical Impact:** Community gatherings; best time for hiring laborers
- **Adventuring:** Good time to stock supplies; communities welcoming

### Deity-Specific Holidays

#### Followers of the Radiant Queen (Light, Justice)
**Day of Reckoning** (Summer Solstice)
- Public declarations of justice served
- Settling of disputes
- Amnesty for minor offences confessed openly

#### Followers of the Stone father (Craft, Endurance)
**Forgefire Festival** (Mid-Winter)
- Craftsmen display their finest work
- Competitions for best metalwork, stonework
- Apprentices gain full status

#### Followers of the Verdant Mother (Nature, Growth)
**Green Awakening** (Spring Equinox)
- Planting ceremonies
- Wild celebrations in forests
- Blessing of seeds and livestock

#### Followers of the Silent Watcher (Death, Memory)
**Night of Remembrance** (Autumn full moon)
- Honoring the dead
- Speaking names of the departed
- Visiting graves and offering memories

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote RELIGIOUS PRACTICES IN AEVORIA}}

\page

### Festival Opportunities

Religious festivals create opportunities for characters:

**Social Connections**
- Festivals are excellent times to meet NPCs
- Community bonds strengthen during shared observances
- Outsiders who participate respectfully gain acceptance

**Commercial Activity**
- Special markets during major festivals
- Increased demand for entertainment, luxury goods
- Opportunities for merchants and traders

**Temple Relationships**
- Attending services and participating respectfully builds goodwill
- Donations during festivals are noticed and appreciated
- May unlock special blessings or assistance

**Adventure Hooks**
- Festivals can be targets for thieves, cultists, or monsters
- Missing persons often noticed during gatherings
- Old grudges may surface during emotional occasions

### Holiday Calendar by Season

**Winter**
- The Long Night (solstice)
- Forgefire Festival (Stonefather, mid-winter)
- Festival of Quiet Reflection (Silent Watcher, new moon)

**Spring**
- First Thaw (early spring)
- Green Awakening (equinox, Verdant Mother)
- Day of Contracts (late spring, merchant blessing)

**Summer**
- Day of Reckoning (solstice, Radiant Queen)
- Sea Wind Festival (coastal regions)
- Storm Moon Dancing (wild magic celebration)

**Autumn**
- Harvest Moon (equinox, universal)
- Night of Remembrance (full moon, Silent Watcher)
- Vintner's Blessing (wine harvest)

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote RELIGIOUS PRACTICES IN AEVORIA}}

\page

## Divine Magic in Society

### How Common Folk View Magic

**Arcane vs. Divine**
People trust divine magic more than arcane:
- Divine magic comes from gods (understood and sanctioned)
- Arcane magic comes from study or pacts (mysterious and potentially dangerous)
- Clerics are community members; wizards are outsiders or specialists

**Trust in Temple Magic**
- Healing from temples is reliable and safe
- Divine guidance through Augury or Divination is respected (though costly)
- Curses removed by clerics are truly gone (not suppressed)

**Skepticism Varies**
- **High:** Vharoxis (question everything)
- **Moderate:** Urban areas (magic is a tool like any other)
- **Low:** Frontier (magic is rare enough to inspire awe and trust)

### Clerics and Paladins as Authorities

Divine spellcasters hold unofficial authority:

**Social Status**
- Clerics are respected community leaders
- Paladins are viewed as champions and protectors
- Both expected to act morally and help those in need

**Expectations**
- Will heal the injured (for appropriate donation or free if poor)
- Will investigate supernatural threats
- Will mediate disputes fairly
- Will share religious wisdom

**Privileges**
- Given benefit of the doubt in disputes
- Offered hospitality freely
- Sought for counsel and guidance

**Responsibilities**
- Must maintain alignment and divine favor
- Expected to serve community, not just self
- Failures in duty damage reputation significantly

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote RELIGIOUS PRACTICES IN AEVORIA}}

\page

### Temples as Safe Havens

Temples serve as more than houses of worship:

**Community Centers**
- Meeting spaces for important gatherings
- Archives of community history and records
- Schools for basic education (literacy, math, history)

**Social Services**
- Food distribution to the poor
- Orphan care
- Elder support
- Disaster relief

**Information Networks**
- Temples communicate with each other across regions
- Clergy often know about threats, opportunities, news
- May share information with trusted adventurers

**Neutral Ground**
- Disputes can be mediated on temple grounds
- Violence in temples is deeply taboo
- Conflicting parties can meet safely

### Divine Magic and the Law

**Legal Status**
- Divine magic is legal and encouraged throughout Aevoria
- Exception: Vharoxis has no formal stance; anything goes
- Some spells (Speak with Dead, Zone of Truth) may be used in trials

**Restrictions**
- Resurrection magic requires temple approval (prevents abuse)
- Certain curses and dark miracles are forbidden
- Raising undead is universally condemned (evil act)

**Divine Judgment**
In serious matters, divine magic may be invoked:
- Zone of Truth in trials (expensive, rare)
- Augury to guide investigations
- Commune for questions of law interpretation (extremely rare)

Cost and rarity mean divine magic is saved for truly significant cases.

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote RELIGIOUS PRACTICES IN AEVORIA}}

\page

## Interfaith Relations

Aevoria's pantheon is large, and most people worship multiple deities depending on circumstances.

### Religious Tolerance

**Generally Tolerant**
Most regions allow worship of any deity in the common pantheon:
- Temples of different faiths coexist peacefully
- People pray to different gods for different needs
- Multi-faith households are common

**Regional Preferences**
- **Solaris Dominion:** Strong preference for Radiant Queen; other faiths tolerated
- **Divinity's Beacon:** All faiths welcome; city is neutral ground
- **Stonebound Depths:** Overwhelmingly Stonefather worship; respectful of others
- **Nullwood Expanse:** Verdant Mother dominant; imported faiths viewed with suspicion

### Conflicting Philosophies

Some tensions exist between faiths:

**Covenant of the Silent Vigil vs. Unregulated Magic**
- The Covenant opposes unaccountable arcane power
- Friction with some arcane traditions and Vharoxis culture

**Life/Death Domain Tension**
- Followers of life-focused deities vs. death domain worshippers
- Philosophical disagreement rather than open conflict
- Both respected if approached with honor

**Civilization vs. Wilderness**
- City-building faiths vs. nature-focused worship
- Usually resolved through mutual respect and compromise

**Lawful vs. Chaotic Deities**
- Different visions of ideal society
- Rarely leads to violence; more like political disagreement

### Heresy and Apostasy

**Rare but Serious**
True heresy (worshipping evil entities, dark pacts) is condemned:
- Demonic pacts
- Undead worship
- Evil deities (if they exist—debated by scholars)

**Enforcement**
- Covenant of the Silent Vigil investigates reports
- Local authorities handle obvious cases
- Serious matters may involve divine intervention (rarely)

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote RELIGIOUS PRACTICES IN AEVORIA}}

\page

## Religious Practices by Region

### Northreach (Frontier)

**Character:** Practical, survival-focused faith
- **Common Prayers:** Protection, safe travel, good weather
- **Temple Frequency:** Every 2-3 settlements; circuit priests common
- **Observance Level:** Moderate; people pray when needed
- **Local Custom:** Offering food/drink to travelers (sacred hospitality)

### Solaris Dominion (Cultural Capital)

**Character:** Organized, ceremonial faith
- **Common Prayers:** Justice, prosperity, artistic inspiration
- **Temple Frequency:** Multiple temples in every city
- **Observance Level:** High; regular attendance expected
- **Local Custom:** Eclipse Day silence (commemorates historical event)

### Nullwood Expanse (Elven Homeland)

**Character:** Memory-focused, living faith
- **Common Prayers:** Ancestors, nature balance, memory preservation
- **Temple Frequency:** Sacred groves rather than building temples
- **Observance Level:** High but private; faith integrated with daily life
- **Local Custom:** Speaking memories aloud to preserve them

### Stonebound Depths (Dwarven Homeland)

**Character:** Traditional, craft-focused faith
- **Common Prayers:** Ancestors, craft quality, stone stability
- **Temple Frequency:** Hall-shrines in every community
- **Observance Level:** Very high; faith inseparable from culture
- **Local Custom:** Resonance-testing before major decisions

### Vharoxis (Outlaw City)

**Character:** Individual, unorganized spirituality
- **Common Prayers:** Personal success, protection from betrayal
- **Temple Frequency:** None (traditional); independent shrines
- **Observance Level:** Low to moderate; highly personalized
- **Local Custom:** Mask offerings (leave old masks at personal shrines)

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote RELIGIOUS PRACTICES IN AEVORIA}}

\page

### Emberlands (Disaster Zone)

**Character:** Desperate, community-focused faith
- **Common Prayers:** Survival, renewal, strength
- **Temple Frequency:** Temporary shelters and mobile priests
- **Observance Level:** Very high; people turn to faith in crisis
- **Local Custom:** Sharing fire (communal flames represent hope)

### Verdant Marches (Fertile Farmland)

**Character:** Seasonal, nature-aligned faith
- **Common Prayers:** Good harvests, gentle weather, healthy livestock
- **Temple Frequency:** Village temples, harvest shrines
- **Observance Level:** Moderate to high; tied to agricultural calendar
- **Local Custom:** First harvest offerings (community feasts)

### Shattered Coast (Maritime Region)

**Character:** Superstitious, safety-focused faith
- **Common Prayers:** Safe voyages, calm seas, good fishing
- **Temple Frequency:** Port temples, lighthouse shrines
- **Observance Level:** Moderate; sailors are devout out of necessity
- **Local Custom:** Never set sail without blessing

### Divinity's Beacon (Holy City)

**Character:** Universal, scholarly faith
- **Common Prayers:** Varies widely by visitor and resident
- **Temple Frequency:** Highest concentration in Aevoria
- **Observance Level:** Very high; city's purpose is religious
- **Local Custom:** Hospitality to pilgrims; answering theological questions

### Sunken Dominion (Underwater Realms)

**Character:** Adapted, water-focused faith
- **Common Prayers:** Safe tides, protection from deep things, communication
- **Temple Frequency:** Underwater grottos and surface docks
- **Observance Level:** High in settlements; varies for nomads
- **Local Custom:** Offerings cast into deep water

### The Far North (Arctic Frontier)

**Character:** Survival-focused, ancestor-honoring faith
- **Common Prayers:** Warmth, endurance, safe hunting
- **Temple Frequency:** Rare; mobile shamans and family shrines
- **Observance Level:** Very high; survival requires divine favor
- **Local Custom:** Story-songs to honor ancestors

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote RELIGIOUS PRACTICES IN AEVORIA}}

\page

## Religion and Your Character

### Building Religious Background

Consider these questions for your character:

**Faith Level**
- Devout believer (regular temple attendance, daily prayer)
- Casual follower (pray when needed, attend major festivals)
- Respectful skeptic (go through motions for community)
- Secular/agnostic (acknowledge gods exist, don't worship)

**Regional Influence**
- How does your home region's religious culture shape you?
- Do you follow regional traditions or rebel against them?

**Personal Experiences**
- Has prayer ever been answered in your character's life?
- Have you witnessed divine magic?
- Do you trust temple authority?

**Practical Matters**
- Which deity do you invoke for different needs?
- Do you carry religious tokens or symbols?
- How does your class affect your faith?

### Clerics and Paladins

If you're playing a divine caster:

**Choose Your Deity Carefully**
- Alignment must match your deity's requirements
- Domain choice should reflect deity's portfolio
- Background should explain your calling

**Define Your Relationship**
- How did you receive your calling?
- Do you serve a specific temple or wander?
- What does your deity expect from you?

**Plan for Conflicts**
- Your oath/faith may conflict with party goals
- Some NPCs distrust or test divine casters
- Failing your deity has mechanical consequences

### Non-Divine Characters

Even if you're not a cleric or paladin:

**Temple Interaction**
- You may need healing or services
- Temples are good sources of information
- Building temple relationships opens opportunities

**Respect vs. Belief**
- You don't have to be devout to be respectful
- Disrespecting temples makes enemies
- Understanding local customs prevents mistakes

---

## Adventure Hooks Related to Faith

**Temple Needs**
- Temples hire adventurers for dangerous tasks (retrieving relics, protecting pilgrims)
- Investigation of supernatural threats
- Escorting clerics to dangerous areas

**Religious Conflicts**
- Heresy investigations
- Rival faiths competing for influence
- Desecrated temples needing cleansing

**Holy Quests**
- Recovering lost sacred texts
- Destroying evil artifacts
- Establishing new temples in frontier regions

**Festival Problems**
- Security for major gatherings
- Missing pilgrims
- Disrupted ceremonies

---

*For detailed information about specific deities, see the Gods and Religion chapter.*

*For information about the Covenant of the Silent Vigil, see the Organizations chapter.*

# Places of Legend

<!-- FILE_START: ../World Building/Locations/Divinitys_Beacon.md -->
# Divinity's Beacon

Status: **world canon (off-map)**. Not located in Northreach.

**Region:** Solaris Dominion

## Concept
A major holy city that welcomes all good-aligned gods (no single state religion), but still stands in ideological opposition to permissive arcane enclaves—especially communities that shelter warlocks or tolerate morally gray magic.

## Built-in party tension
- Paladins/clerics can have roots and allies here.
- Wizards/warlocks may be viewed with suspicion depending on patron, methods, and past deeds.

## See also
- Pantheon details: See **Chapter 6: Gods and Religion**

\page
<!-- FILE_END: ../World Building/Locations/Divinitys_Beacon.md -->

<!-- FILE_START: ../World Building/Locations/Solace_Nexus.md -->
# Solace Nexus — Ley-Port City of Magic

Status: **world canon (off-map)**. Not located in Northreach.

**Region:** The Verdant Marches

Solace Nexus is a warm southern valley-city that functions like a **harbor for ley lines**—a place where travelers, merchants, scholars, and opportunists “dock” their spells, their curios, and their secrets.

---

## The pitch (what makes it feel different)
- **Not a seaport**: Solace Nexus is wealthy without ships, because its true trade moves on **arcane currents**.
- **A ley-port**: people don’t come for fish or timber; they come for **convergence**, for safe spellwork, for rare reagents, for shortcuts in distance and knowledge.
- **A city built on containment**: almost everything civic—roads, plazas, laws, and etiquette—exists to prevent the Nexus from becoming a crater.

---

## Geography & approach
Solace Nexus sits in a **sun-warmed valley** ringed by steep, broken highlands. The routes in are few and difficult:

- **The Red Switchbacks**: a winding mule-road cut into sun-baked stone, famous for mirages and “helpful” echoes that mimic your companions’ voices.
- **The Verdant Cut**: a narrow pass through thick, flowering growth where spores cling to spell components and change their behavior.
- **The Skyrail Ruins**: ancient pylons span a ravine; locals insist the “rails” still exist, but only during certain weather.

### The Nexus Phenomenon
At the valley’s center is a mild, constant sensation like pressure behind the eyes—subtle for most, unmistakable for casters. Locals call it:

- **the Hush** (when the air goes unnaturally quiet before a surge)
- **the Pulse** (a rolling wave of warmth/cold as leys rebalance)
- **the Blue Hour** (twilight when spell-light clings to stone)

---

## City layout (districts)
Solace Nexus is built in rings around a civic core.

### 1) The Concourse (civic core)
Broad plazas etched with non-reactive ward-stone. Public spellcasting is allowed here **only within marked circles**.

Key sites:
- **The Meridian Steps**: a terraced forum where disputes are arbitrated and licenses are granted.
- **The Neutral Font**: a shallow pool that “drinks” small magical residues; citizens toss in spilled cantrips like sweeping dust.

### 2) Scriptor’s Row (trade + scholarship)
An orderly district of paper-makers, ink-brewers, rune-engravers, lens-crafters, and binderies.

Key sites:
- **The Quiet Index**: a public archive with strict silence, timed entry, and anti-theft wards.
- **The Ink Kitchens**: a block of shops where every alley smells like iron, citrus, ash, or rain.

### 3) The Crucible Wards (alchemy + enchanting)
Heavy stone buildings with vent-stacks and “blast shutters.” Streets are wide enough for carts of sand and water barrels.

Key sites:
- **The Glassworks**: produces ampoules, lenses, and spell-safe containers.
- **The Salt Foundry**: turns mundane salts into stabilizers, binding powders, and ward-paste.

### 4) The Lattice (residential ring)
Homes and courtyards built around micro-wards. Doorways are marked with **small civic seals** that indicate what kinds of spellwork are permitted inside.

Key sites:
- **The Warm Courts**: sheltered communal courtyards with heated stone benches and story-nights.
- **The Mendery**: a neighborhood clinic where mundane medicine and gentle magic share the same shelves.

### 5) The Underways (service tunnels + hidden streets)
Old maintenance tunnels and flood channels. Officially, they exist for civic workers and ward-inspectors.

Unofficially, they’re where:
- illicit summoners meet clients,
- stolen scrolls change hands,
- and pact-makers whisper promises.

---

## Governance & law (the city’s “spell safety code”)
Solace Nexus is run by **the Meridian Council**, a civic body that treats magic like fire in a wooden city: useful, sacred, and regulated.

### Civic licenses
Most working casters carry one of these:
- **Lantern License**: minor spellwork; harmless utility and apprentices.
- **Keystone License**: professional-grade magic; regulated materials and periodic inspection.
- **Vault License**: restricted arts (summoning, binding, significant transmutation); requires a sponsor and heavy oversight.

### Three laws everyone repeats
1) **Cast inside the circle.**
2) **Name your witness.** (serious magic requires an accountable observer)
3) **Pay the ward-tax.** (everyone benefits from containment)

### Enforcement
The city’s arcane peacekeepers are called **Wardens of the Meridian** (not affiliated with Northwatch Wardens).

They use practical tools:
- dampening manacles,
- chalk-seals,
- disruption chimes,
- and trained “sniffers” (people who can sense active magic like a scent).

---

## Factions (power centers)
Pick 2–3 as active at any given time.

### The Meridian Council (civic)
Stability-first bureaucrats. They believe the city survives only because magic is **contained and audited**.

### The Collegia of Lenses (academic)
Researchers, surveyors of ley behavior, and builders of instruments. They fund expeditions and publish “safe” findings.

### The Guild of Quiet Hands (trade)
Scribes, component brokers, artificers, and carriers. They protect the supply chain and quietly decide who gets access to what.

### The Salt & Ember Compact (industrial)
Alchemists and foundry-masters. They keep the city running and will burn neighborhoods before they let a reaction spread.

### The Night Concord (shadow)
A network of pact-brokers, warlocks, and oath-makers who claim they “provide options for those the Council would starve.”

---

## Economy (wizard-adjacent, by design)
Solace Nexus profits off the wizard community—but it’s not only wizards.

### What the city exports
- **Scrollwork**: reliable, standardized scrolls and sealed spell-pages.
- **Stabilized components**: measured reagents packaged with usage notes.
- **Ward-stone**: treated stone tiles that hold a charge without warping.
- **Lenscraft**: prisms, scry-safe glass, reading lenses, and “spell glare” filters.

### What the city imports
- Raw herbs, salts, and minerals.
- Livestock and grain (valley farms exist, but the city outgrows them).
- Rare curios (often acquired via questionable channels).

### Money & barter
Coin is common, but the city also uses **ward-chits** (tax tokens) and **script** (credit slips backed by guilds).

---

## Culture (how it feels to walk the streets)
- Street lamps are hooded with **glare-wards**.
- Many doorways carry tiny inscriptions: “No flame. No calling. No shaping.”
- People greet each other with practical phrases like “Clear circles,” or “May your ink stay true.”
- Children learn chalk geometry before cursive; drawing circles is as normal as tying shoes.

### Festivals
- **The Blue Hour Fair**: once per season, sanctioned demonstrations of safe magic, instrument shows, and story contests.
- **Ledgerturn**: the annual reset of licenses; a week of audits, bribes, public protests, and quiet disappearances.

---

## The shadow layer (warlocks, old pacts, and consequences)
Rumors of darker alleys and hidden circles are true—just not uniformly.

### The pact-market reality
Not everyone here becomes a warlock. But Solace Nexus is where desperate people come when:
- the Council denies a license,
- a family debt threatens to ruin them,
- or an illness won’t respond to ordinary cures.

The **Night Concord** offers “solutions”:
- patrons who speak through mirrors,
- contracts inked in saltwater,
- vows sworn over a still-burning candle.

### The city’s oldest secret
People say: “Old pacts were made here, and the consequences still echo.”

In practice, that can mean:
- a neighborhood where luck runs thin,
- a generational curse disguised as tradition,
- or a civic ward that was built on a bargain no one remembers.

---

## Running Solace Nexus at the table

### What problems happen here (scene types)
- A ward-circle is subtly sabotaged, causing a “safe” spell to misbehave.
- A famous scrollwright is blackmailed with proof of illegal work.
- The Collegia’s instrument detects a new ley pattern; everyone wants to control the discovery.
- A pact-broker offers the party what they want—at a cost they can’t yet measure.

### 10 quick locations (drop-in)
1) A bookstore that only sells books copied by hand—no originals.
2) A component shop with a “smell wall” where jars are unlabelled to avoid theft.
3) A public casting plaza with circles worn smooth as river stones.
4) A bathhouse heated by bound steam-elementals (licensed, allegedly).
5) A rooftop garden where herbs grow in geometric beds that echo ward patterns.
6) A tavern that forbids spellcasting but sells “spell-safe” drinks anyway.
7) A quiet chapel that treats oaths as sacred, not gods.
8) A night market under a bridge where masks are mandatory.
9) A clinic with two lines: mundane triage and “arcane contamination.”
10) A tunnel door with a fresh chalk-circle drawn on it every morning.

### 8 rumors (useful and messy)
1) “The Neutral Font is filling up. That’s not supposed to happen.”
2) “Someone forged a Vault License, and the Council is terrified.”
3) “A new patron is buying names. Just names.”
4) “A whole block is warded wrong—like it was built upside down.”
5) “The Collegia has a map of the ley lines. It changes when you blink.”
6) “There’s a doorway in the Underways that opens when you apologize sincerely.”
7) “Ink from the Ink Kitchens can write things you don’t know yet.”
8) “The Wardens of the Meridian don’t sleep; they trade shifts with mirrors.”

### 6 encounter seeds
1) A courier begs the party to deliver a sealed scroll—then someone tries to steal the seal, not the scroll.
2) A ward-inspector collapses mid-audit; their notes show a pattern that points to sabotage.
3) A small summoning goes wrong in a rented room; the landlord blames the party for being “obviously magical.”
4) A guild auction erupts when a bidder recognizes the party as outsiders and assumes they’re undercover.
5) A pact-broker offers a “free” favor to prove sincerity; the favor is harmless but reputationally poisonous.
6) A Blue Hour demonstration accidentally reveals a hidden sigil under the plaza stones.

---

## Design notes (for future you)
- Keep Solace Nexus useful as a **hub**: information, components, licenses, patrons, and politics.
- Let the city feel safe until it suddenly isn’t; the tension is “civilization held together by chalk and etiquette.”
- The shadow layer works best when it’s *plausible*—pacts aren’t everywhere, but they’re always an option.

\page

## Travel Times

### From Waystone Inn (Guild Headquarters)

| Destination | Distance | Travel Time | Road Quality |
|:------------|:---------|:------------|:-------------|
| **Welton** (Southwest) | ~30 miles | 1–2 days | Fair; rural road |
| **Westly's Farm** (via Welton) | ~35 miles | 2–3 days | Poor; farm track |
| **Pinebrook** (Southeast) | ~45 miles | 2–3 days | Fair; trade route |
| **Noke's Tower** (West) | ~8 miles | ½–1 day | Good; river path |
| **Palebank Village** (Northeast) | ~60 miles | 3–5 days | Poor; coastal trail |
| **Temple of the Dragonknights** (Northwest) | ~80 miles | 5–7 days | Poor; mountain trail |

### Travel Modifiers

**Weather Conditions:**
- **Clear Weather:** Standard travel times
- **Light Rain/Snow:** +1 day per 3 days of travel
- **Heavy Weather:** +1 day per day of travel; may require shelter
- **Winter Storms:** Travel may become impossible; seek shelter immediately

**Party Composition:**
- **Small Party (2–4):** Standard travel times
- **Large Party (5+):** +10% travel time
- **Mounted Party:** –20% travel time on good roads
- **With Wagons:** +50% travel time; poor roads may be impassable

## Lodging & Meals

### Inn Prices (Standard)

| Service | Cost | Notes |
|:--------|:-----|:------|
| **Squalid Room** | 7 cp/night | Shared room, thin bedrolls, no privacy |
| **Poor Room** | 1 sp/night | Shared room, basic beds, minimal comfort |
| **Modest Room** | 5 sp/night | Private room, clean bed, simple furnishings |
| **Comfortable Room** | 8 sp/night | Private room, good bed, secure lock |
| **Wealthy Room** | 2 gp/night | Fine room, quality furnishings, excellent service |
| **Aristocratic Suite** | 4 gp/night | Best rooms, luxury furnishings (rare in frontier) |

### Meal Prices

| Meal Type | Cost | What You Get |
|:----------|:-----|:-------------|
| **Squalid Meal** | 3 cp | Bread, thin soup, questionable quality |
| **Poor Meal** | 6 cp | Porridge, bread, small beer |
| **Modest Meal** | 3 sp | Stew, bread, cheese, ale or cider |
| **Comfortable Meal** | 5 sp | Roast meat, vegetables, good bread, wine |
| **Wealthy Meal** | 8 sp | Multiple courses, fine wine, dessert |
| **Banquet** | 10 gp/person | Feast with entertainment (special occasions) |

### Waystone Inn (Warden Headquarters)

**Warden Members:** Modest lodging and meals provided at **no cost** while on active contracts

**Non-Members:**
- **Lodging:** 5 sp/night (modest room)
- **Meals:** 3 sp (modest meal), 5 sp (comfortable meal)
- **Stabling:** 5 cp/night per mount
- **Wagon Storage:** 1 sp/night

**Atmosphere:** Professional, warm, neutral ground

\column

### The Shepherd's Crook Inn (Welton)

**Standard Pricing:**
- **Lodging:** 4 sp/night (modest room)
- **Meals:** 2 sp (modest meal)
- **Stabling:** 3 cp/night per mount

**Special Notes:**
- Prices rise when rumors of danger spread (+50% during emergencies)
- Good source of local gossip and news
- Popular with farmers and traders

### Pinebrook Trade Post

**Standard Pricing:**
- **Lodging:** 6 sp/night (modest to comfortable)
- **Meals:** 3–4 sp (modest meal)
- **Stabling:** 5 cp/night per mount

**Special Notes:**
- Trading hub; slightly higher prices
- Better selection of goods than Welton
- More transient population

### Palebank Village

**Standard Pricing:**
- **Lodging:** 4 sp/night (poor to modest)
- **Meals:** 2 sp (modest meal, fish-heavy)
- **Stabling:** Limited (most use fishing boats)

**Special Notes:**
- Coastal settlement; fresh seafood
- Cold and isolated; fewer amenities
- Prices can spike during bad weather

## Spellcasting Services

### Availability in Northreach

**Magic is rare in the frontier.** Most settlements have no resident spellcasters. The Northwatch Wardens maintain the most reliable access to magical services in the region.

### Waystone Inn (Warden Resources)

**Lorewarden Elric Vael** can provide limited spellcasting services to active Wardens:

| Spell | Level | Cost | Availability |
|:------|:------|:-----|:-------------|
| **Cure Wounds** | 1st | Free (Wardens) | Common |
| **Identify** | 1st | Free (Wardens) | Common |
| **Detect Magic** | 1st | Free (Wardens) | Common |
| **Lesser Restoration** | 2nd | 20 gp | Uncommon |
| **Remove Curse** | 3rd | 50 gp | Rare |
| **Greater Restoration** | 5th | 200 gp | Very Rare |
| **Raise Dead** | 5th | 500 gp + diamonds | Extremely Rare |

**Notes:**
- Non-Wardens pay double
- Higher-level spells may require special request
- Elric prioritizes contract-related needs

### Temple Services (Welton, Pinebrook)

**Small frontier shrines** may offer basic healing:

| Service | Cost | Notes |
|:--------|:-----|:------|
| **Cure Wounds** | 10 gp | If shrine priest available |
| **Lesser Restoration** | 40 gp | Rare; traveling priests only |
| **Blessing/Guidance** | Donation | Common; suggested 1 sp–1 gp |

**Availability:** Inconsistent; frontier has few resident clerics

### Black Market (Pinebrook, Major Settlements)

**Illegal or gray-market magical services** exist but carry risk:

- Prices negotiable (often inflated)
- Quality uncertain
- May attract unwanted attention
- DM discretion on availability

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote PLAYER QUICK REFERENCE GUIDE}}

\page

## Frontier Conditions

### Northreach Modifiers

**The frontier is not the city.** Prices, availability, and services differ from core D&D assumptions.

### Price Adjustments

| Item Category | Modifier | Reason |
|:--------------|:---------|:-------|
| **Basic Supplies** | Standard | Locally produced |
| **Imported Goods** | +50% | Long supply chains |
| **Luxury Items** | +100% | Rare; high demand |
| **Magic Items** | +200% | Extremely scarce |
| **Cold Weather Gear** | Standard | Locally essential |
| **Emergency Supplies** | +100–300% | Demand spikes during crisis |

### Availability Guide

**Common:** Available in most settlements (Waystone Inn, Welton, Pinebrook)

**Uncommon:** Available at larger settlements or by special order (1–3 days)

**Rare:** Only at Waystone Inn or major trade hubs; may require travel to larger cities

**Very Rare:** Special order; weeks or months to acquire

**Legendary:** Not available in Northreach; requires expedition to distant cities

### Seasonal Variations

Northreach experiences harsh seasonal changes that affect travel, prices, and services.

#### Winter (Late Fall through Early Spring — ~6 months)

- **Travel Times:** +50% due to snow and ice
- **Food Prices:** +25% (limited fresh produce)
- **Cold Weather Gear:** Essential for survival
- **Road Conditions:** Poor to impassable
- **Services:** Limited; many craftsmen stay indoors

#### Summer (Late Spring through Early Fall — ~4 months)

- **Travel Times:** Standard
- **Food Prices:** Standard to –10% (harvest season)
- **Road Conditions:** Fair to good
- **Services:** Widely available

#### Mud Season (Spring & Fall Transitions — ~2 months total)

- **Travel:** Variable; roads can be worse than winter
- **Prices:** Standard
- **Services:** Preparing for next season; inconsistent availability

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote PLAYER QUICK REFERENCE GUIDE}}

\page

### Local Customs & Expectations

#### Frontier Etiquette

**Hospitality:**
- Travelers are offered basic shelter in emergencies
- Repay kindness with labor, coin, or future aid
- Never abuse hospitality; reputation matters

**Trade:**
- Haggling is expected for large purchases
- Fair weights and honest prices are valued
- Cheating or stealing brings harsh consequences

**Neutrality:**
- The Waystone Inn is neutral ground
- Starting fights at the inn is forbidden
- Marshal Thorne enforces this strictly

**Community Aid:**
- Settlers help neighbors survive
- Wardens are expected to assist in emergencies
- Refusing aid to those in need damages reputation

#### Currency Notes

**Standard Exchange Rates:**
- 1 gold piece (gp) = 10 silver pieces (sp)
- 1 silver piece (sp) = 10 copper pieces (cp)
- 1 gold piece (gp) = 100 copper pieces (cp)

**Practical Use in Northreach:**
- **Copper:** Daily expenses (meals, stabling, small goods)
- **Silver:** Lodging, services, local trade
- **Gold:** Major purchases, contracts, wages
- **Platinum:** Rarely seen; exotic transactions only

**Barter is Common:**
- Many frontier folk trade goods directly
- Wardens can often trade service for supplies
- Some settlements prefer trade goods to coin

---

## Quick Notes for Players

**Always Carry:**
- Rope (50 ft minimum)
- Torches or lantern with oil
- Rations (3 days minimum)
- Waterskin
- Cold weather gear (during cold months)
- Tinderbox

**Before Leaving Waystone Inn:**
- Check contract details
- Confirm travel time and route
- Ensure adequate supplies
- Note nearest settlements for resupply
- Report expected return date

**In the Field:**
- Weather can change rapidly
- Settlements are days apart
- Magic is unreliable
- Wildlife is dangerous
- Trust your instincts

**Emergency Protocol:**
- Return to nearest settlement
- Send word to Waystone Inn
- Request reinforcements if needed
- Wardens support each other

---

*"The frontier rewards preparation and punishes carelessness. Know your limits. Know your route. Know when to retreat."*  
— **Marshal Brenna Thorne**, Northwatch Wardens

# Currency and Trade in Northreach


## Overview

In Northreach, money flows as slowly as news travels. The frontier economy runs on practical needs: food, tools, shelter, and protection. Gold matters, but reputation and relationships often matter more.

---

## Standard Currency

### The Five Coins

Northreach uses the standard coinage found throughout the known world:

- **Copper Pieces (cp):** The worker's coin. Most daily transactions.
- **Silver Pieces (sp):** Common currency. Fair wages and modest goods.
- **Electrum Pieces (ep):** Rare in Northreach. Mistrusted by some.
- **Gold Pieces (gp):** Serious money. Major purchases and contracts.
- **Platinum Pieces (pp):** Almost never seen. Merchant caravans and wealthy travelers.

### Exchange Rates

Standard rates apply:
- 10 copper = 1 silver
- 2 electrum = 1 gold
- 10 silver = 1 gold
- 10 gold = 1 platinum

### What Money Looks Like Here

**Worn and Mixed:**
- Coins from many kingdoms circulate
- Age and wear common (no mints nearby)
- Value by metal content, not whose face is stamped on it
- Clipped or shaved coins viewed with suspicion

**Local Preferences:**
- Silver most common for daily business
- Gold saved for emergencies or major purchases
- Copper used for smallest transactions
- Platinum might sit in a merchant's strongbox for years

---

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote CURRENCY AND TRADE IN NORTHREACH}}

\page

## The Practical Economy

### What Things Cost

#### Food and Lodging
- **Meal (common):** 3 cp (stew, bread, ale)
- **Meal (good):** 5 sp (meat, fresh bread, wine)
- **Lodging (common):** 5 sp per night (shared room, straw mattress)
- **Lodging (private):** 1 gp per night (private room, real bed)
- **Week's rations:** 5 sp (preserved food, travels well)
- **Fresh meat:** 2 sp per pound (when available)
- **Loaf of bread:** 2 cp
- **Mug of ale:** 4 cp
- **Bottle of wine (decent):** 1 gp

#### Tools and Equipment
- **Common tools:** 2 gp (hammer, saw, axe)
- **Specialist tools:** 5-25 gp (carpenter's tools, smith's tools)
- **Rope (50 ft):** 1 gp
- **Lantern:** 5 sp
- **Oil (flask):** 1 sp
- **Warm clothing:** 2 gp (essential for winter)
- **Winter cloak (fur-lined):** 10 gp
- **Sturdy boots:** 2 gp (life-or-death equipment)

#### Animals and Transport
- **Draft horse:** 50 gp (working animal)
- **Riding horse:** 75 gp (faster, requires more care)
- **Mule:** 8 gp (hardy, handles cold better)
- **Ox:** 15 gp (strongest, slowest)
- **Cart:** 15 gp
- **Wagon:** 35 gp
- **Sled:** 5 gp (winter essential)

\column

#### Labor and Services
- **Unskilled labor:** 2 sp per day (farm work, hauling)
- **Skilled labor:** 2 gp per day (carpenter, blacksmith)
- **Expert services:** 5-10 gp per day (engineer, specialist)
- **Guide services:** 5 sp per day (local trails)
- **Dangerous escort:** 2 gp per day (armed protection)
- **Healing (minor):** 1 gp (cure light wounds)
- **Healing (serious):** 10 gp+ (disease, poison, restoration)

### Seasonal Price Variations

**Spring:**
- Food prices drop as stores are sold before spoiling
- Labor costs rise (planting season)
- Travel becomes possible again

**Summer:**
- Stable prices
- Trade caravans arrive from south
- Best time for major purchases

**Autumn:**
- Food prices rise (preservation season)
- Tools in high demand (winter preparation)
- Smart buyers stock up now

**Winter:**
- Everything costs more
- Fresh food scarce or unavailable
- Travel dangerous and expensive
- Communities rely on stored goods

---

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote CURRENCY AND TRADE IN NORTHREACH}}

\page

## Trade Routes and Networks

### The Waystone Hub

**Waystone Inn sits at the practical center of trade:**
- Northeast to Palebank Village (3-5 days)
- Southwest to Welton (1-2 days)
- Southeast to Pinebrook (2-3 days)
- West to Noke's Tower (½-1 day)

### Trade Goods

#### What Northreach Exports
**Furs and Hides:**
- Winter pelts (high quality)
- Leather (workable)
- Exotic furs (rare predators)
- Value: 5 sp to 50 gp depending on quality

**Timber:**
- Construction lumber
- Specialty woods
- Firewood (local use)
- Value: Varies by type and quantity

**Minerals (when found):**
- Iron ore
- Copper
- Semi-precious stones
- Value: Depends on discovery and purity

**Preserved Foods:**
- Smoked meats
- Dried fish (from Palebank)
- Preserved vegetables
- Value: 1-5 sp per pound

\column

#### What Northreach Imports
**Metal Goods:**
- Tools (axes, saws, plows)
- Weapons and armor
- Nails and hardware
- Cookware

**Textiles:**
- Quality cloth
- Heavy wool
- Rope and cordage
- Canvas

**Luxury Items:**
- Spices
- Salt (preservation essential)
- Sugar (rare)
- Tea and coffee
- Books and paper

**Specialized Equipment:**
- Alchemical supplies
- Magical components
- Medicines
- Professional tools

### Trading Caravans

**Summer Caravans:**
- Arrive late spring, leave before first snow
- Bring southern goods
- Take northern exports
- Major event for settlements
- Prices negotiable (they want to sell before leaving)

**Local Traders:**
- Move between Northreach settlements year-round
- Smaller inventories
- Better knowledge of local needs
- More flexible on payment terms

---

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote CURRENCY AND TRADE IN NORTHREACH}}

\page

## Barter and Alternative Currency

### When Coin Isn't Enough

In Northreach, pure currency transactions are often impractical:

**Common Reasons to Barter:**
- Lack of sufficient coinage
- Need to preserve cash reserves for winter
- Building relationships and obligations
- Items more useful than money in isolation
- Emergency situations where goodwill matters

### What Trades Well

**High-Value Barter Goods:**
- Quality tools (always needed)
- Preserved food (winter insurance)
- Warm clothing and blankets
- Ammunition and weapon maintenance
- Healing supplies
- Salt (preservation essential)
- Seeds (next year's crop)

**Service Barter:**
- Labor exchange (help with barn-raising, harvesting)
- Skill sharing (teach a trade, share knowledge)
- Future obligations (recorded and remembered)
- Protection and escort services
- Information and warnings

### Barter Etiquette

**Fair Exchange:**
- Both parties should feel satisfied
- Consider future value and scarcity
- Account for quality and condition
- Factor in urgency and need

**Recording Trades:**
- Major barter deals witnessed
- Written records for complex exchanges
- Community memory for smaller trades
- Breaking barter agreements damages reputation

\column

### Credit and Debt

**How Credit Works:**
- Based on reputation and relationships
- Witnessed by community members
- Written for significant amounts
- Interest rarely charged among locals
- Expected repayment timeline agreed upon

**When Debts Are Called:**
- Before winter (need to settle accounts)
- Emergency situations
- Debtor preparing to leave area
- When creditor faces hardship

**Consequences of Default:**
- Reputation damage (severe)
- Exclusion from future credit
- Community pressure to repay
- Possible loss of property
- Forced labor to settle debt

### The Favor Economy

**Favors as Currency:**
- Helping neighbors creates obligations
- Remembered for years or generations
- Repaid when able
- Refusing reasonable request damages standing

**Examples:**
- "I helped build your barn; you'll help with mine"
- "Your father saved my life; I owe your family"
- "You warned us about the wolves; we'll remember"
- "We sheltered you through winter; someday we'll need shelter"

---

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote CURRENCY AND TRADE IN NORTHREACH}}

\page

## Guild Contracts and Payment

### Warden Contract Structure

**Standard Contract Terms:**
- Base payment agreed in advance
- Bonus for exceptional results
- Hazard pay for unusual danger
- Expenses covered (within reason)
- Payment on completion
- Failure consequences specified

### Payment Scales

**Low Risk Contracts (1-3 gp per person):**
- Message delivery
- Basic escort
- Simple investigation
- Routine patrol

**Medium Risk Contracts (5-10 gp per person):**
- Dangerous escort
- Monster investigation
- Settlement defense
- Rescue operations

**High Risk Contracts (15-50 gp per person):**
- Major threats
- Extended expeditions
- High-value targets
- Significant danger

**Legendary Contracts (50+ gp per person):**
- Existential threats
- Ancient ruins
- Powerful monsters
- Region-wide consequences

### Payment Methods

**Preferred:**
- Guild vouchers (redeemable at Waystone Inn)
- Mix of coin and supplies
- Advance payment (partial)
- Completion bonus

\column

**Alternative Arrangements:**
- Settlement provides goods instead of coin
- Future considerations (political favors)
- Land grants (rare)
- Salvage rights
- Information access

### The Guild's Cut

**Steward Mara's System:**
- Guild takes 10% administrative fee
- Covers room and board at Waystone
- Includes basic supplies and equipment access
- Provides medical care after missions
- Maintains guild reputation and connections

**What the Fee Covers:**
- Contract verification
- Payment guarantee (guild ensures you're paid)
- Equipment storage
- Training and mentorship access
- Legal support if needed
- Recovery from guild funds if client defaults

## Regional Economic Differences

### Palebank Village

**Economy:**
- Fishing and trapping based
- Regular contact with southern traders (when sea permits)
- Access to coastal goods
- Some wealth from Eiselcross relics

**Currency Notes:**
- More coin circulates than inland settlements
- Relic trade brings occasional wealth
- Winter isolation reduces trade
- Barter still common for daily needs

**Typical Prices:**
- Fish: cheaper and fresher
- Southern goods: available but expensive
- Winter supplies: premium prices (vulnerability)
- Relics: variable (depends on find and buyer)

### Welton

**Economy:**
- Agricultural base
- Food production for region
- Seasonal wealth (post-harvest)
- Limited manufacturing

**Currency Notes:**
- Most wealth in land and livestock
- Cash poor except post-harvest
- Heavy barter economy
- Payment often in food and labor

\column

**Typical Prices:**
- Food: cheaper and more available
- Tools: premium (must be imported)
- Land: value in productive capacity
- Services: often paid in kind

### Pinebrook

**Economy:**
- Trading post atmosphere
- Mixed economy (agriculture and commerce)
- Stopover point for travelers
- Small manufacturing base

**Currency Notes:**
- More balanced mix of coin and barter
- Merchant families have capital
- Credit more common than other settlements
- Outside money flows through regularly

**Typical Prices:**
- Trade goods: fair (competition)
- Lodging: reasonable (multiple options)
- Services: professional rates
- Local goods: market prices

### Waystone Inn

**Economy:**
- Guild headquarters and activity hub
- Regular coin flow from contracts
- Merchants and travelers pass through
- Supplies both guild and travelers

**Currency Notes:**
- Most coin of any location
- Professional services abundant
- Credit available (through guild)
- Prices stable year-round

---

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote CURRENCY AND TRADE IN NORTHREACH}}

\page

## Economic Challenges

### Scarcity and Supply

**The Core Problem:**
- Small population produces limited goods
- Long supply lines from southern centers
- Seasonal isolation compounds issues
- Essential items can become unavailable

**What This Means:**
- Hoarding during shortages (social pressure against)
- Price spikes when supply interrupted
- Innovation in making do with available materials
- Community resource sharing in emergencies

### Cash Flow Issues

**For Individuals:**
- Income irregular (seasonal, contract-based)
- Major expenses (winter supplies) come all at once
- Emergency costs can devastate families
- Saving difficult when living close to edge

**For Communities:**
- Collective resources limited
- Infrastructure improvements difficult to fund
- Dependence on wealthier patrons or guild
- Difficult to attract and retain specialists

### Distance and Isolation

**Transport Costs:**
- Moving goods expensive and dangerous
- Time costs money (guarding caravans)
- Weather can destroy shipments
- Limited capacity (what one wagon can carry)

**Communication Delays:**
- Price information outdated
- Market changes unknown
- Difficult to coordinate large transactions
- Opportunities missed due to distance

\column

### Seasonal Extremes

**Winter Challenges:**
- No new supplies arrive
- Existing goods must last months
- Emergency shortages can't be quickly resolved
- Communities entirely dependent on preparation

**Spring Challenges:**
- Depleted reserves
- Need to fund planting
- Prices unstable
- Health issues from winter deprivation

### External Economic Pressures

**Southern Market Fluctuations:**
- Prices set by distant markets
- No local control over import costs
- Southern problems become northern problems
- Trade goods subject to outside demand

**Political and Military Disruptions:**
- Wars disrupt supply chains
- Refugees strain local resources
- Banditry increases in unstable times
- Trade routes become dangerous

---

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote CURRENCY AND TRADE IN NORTHREACH}}

\page

## Practical Financial Advice

### For Adventurers

**Before Winter:**
- Convert portable wealth to practical supplies
- Secure lodging arrangements early
- Stock preserved food
- Invest in quality cold weather gear
- Pay debts before isolation sets in

**During Winter:**
- Conserve resources carefully
- Avoid unnecessary travel (expensive and dangerous)
- Indoor work and planning
- Maintain equipment for spring

**Spring and Summer:**
- Time to earn and save
- Make major purchases before autumn
- Build relationships for winter shelter
- Stock up gradually rather than last minute

### For Merchants

**Success Strategies:**
- Know what sells in each season
- Build relationships (repeat business)
- Extend credit carefully (check reputation)
- Diversify inventory (don't depend on one good)
- Plan around caravan schedules

**Avoiding Pitfalls:**
- Don't over-extend on credit
- Account for seasonal cash flow
- Maintain emergency reserves
- Insurance through relationships, not gold alone

\column

### For Settlers

**Economic Survival:**
- Produce your own food (reduce cash needs)
- Develop marketable skills (earn coin)
- Build a reputation (access to credit and help)
- Participate in community labor (obligation network)
- Save for emergencies (winter, injury, loss)

**Building Wealth:**
- Improve land gradually
- Acquire quality tools (investment, not expense)
- Raise children as labor force (harsh but true)
- Develop specialty skill (premium income)
- Marry well (combine resources and skills)

---

## Common Financial Sayings

**About Saving:**
- "A silver saved in summer is worth gold in winter."
- "The best time to fix the roof is when the sun is shining."
- "Don't spend your seed corn."

**About Credit:**
- "Debt is a rope: useful until you hang from it."
- "Borrow from a neighbor; owe to a friend; fear a stranger's coin."
- "Credit costs more than coin, even at no interest."

**About Trade:**
- "First caravan of summer charges what the market will bear; last caravan takes what it can get."
- "Never trust a merchant who won't eat his own goods."
- "The buyer needs the seller; the seller needs the buyer; but winter needs neither."

**About Wealth:**
- "Rich in autumn, poor by spring—that's frontier mathematics."
- "A full barn is worth more than a full purse up here."
- "You can't eat gold, but it buys what you can."

---

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote CURRENCY AND TRADE IN NORTHREACH}}

\page

## Banking and Safekeeping

### Where Money Lives

**No Formal Banks:**
- No banking institutions in Northreach
- Secure storage is personal responsibility
- Community solutions for collective funds
- Guild provides limited services for members

**Storage Options:**

**Personal:**
- Hidden caches (buried, concealed)
- Strongboxes (locked, sometimes trapped)
- On person (vulnerable to theft and loss)
- Split between locations (don't keep all in one place)

**Community:**
- Settlement leader's safe (witnessed deposits)
- Church or shrine (priest as keeper)
- Merchant's strongroom (for fee)
- Guild vault (for members)

**Risks:**
- Theft (constant concern)
- Fire (destroys caches)
- Forgetting locations (happens more than admitted)
- Death (wealth lost if location unknown)
- Raids and attacks (why total wealth is often hidden)

### Letters of Credit

**How They Work:**
- Written guarantee of payment
- Requires trusted witness
- Only as good as issuer's reputation
- Must be redeemed before issuer leaves region

**Who Issues:**
- Established merchants
- Guild officers
- Settlement leaders
- Wealthy patrons

\column

**Advantages:**
- Carry wealth without carrying coin
- Safer than gold in purse
- Can be witnessed and recorded
- Serves as contract evidence

**Limitations:**
- Only works with known issuers
- Limited geographic range
- Requires literacy (both parties)
- No mechanism to enforce across regions

---

## Wealth and Social Standing

### What Wealth Means

**Not Simple:**
- Coin alone doesn't determine status
- Competence and contribution matter more
- Wasteful wealth spending looked down upon
- Generosity in need builds reputation

**Respectable Wealth:**
- Productive land
- Quality tools and equipment
- Well-maintained property
- Livestock and draft animals
- Stored provisions
- Useful skills and knowledge

**Suspicious Wealth:**
- Large unexplained sums
- No visible means of support
- Luxury goods inappropriate to station
- Unwillingness to contribute to community
- Wealth without work

### Class and Economy

**Rough Economic Classes:**

**Poor but Surviving:**
- Day laborers
- New settlers
- Young adults starting out
- Recent victims of misfortune

---

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote CURRENCY AND TRADE IN NORTHREACH}}

\page

**Working Comfortable:**
- Established farmers and herders
- Skilled craftspeople
- Experienced laborers
- Most of Northreach population

**Prosperous:**
- Successful merchants
- Master craftspeople
- Large landholders
- Guild officers
- Settlement leaders

**Wealthy (rare):**
- Major merchants
- Landowners with multiple properties
- Successful adventurers who invested well
- Those with southern connections maintaining capital

### Social Mobility

**Possible But Difficult:**
- Hard work alone insufficient
- Requires skill, luck, and opportunity
- Marriage can change economic status
- One bad winter can drop you down
- One good find can elevate you
- Reputation enables advancement

**Barriers to Mobility:**
- Limited capital for investment
- No safety net for failure
- Equipment and land expensive
- Skills take time to develop
- Death and injury common
- Bad luck devastating

---

\column

## Economic Glossary

**Common Terms:**

**"Winter Price":** Premium charged for goods in short supply during winter.

**"Caravan Luck":** When summer traders arrive with exactly what you need.

**"Copper Dreaming":** Planning unrealistic purchases beyond your means.

**"Silver Sense":** Practical financial judgment.

**"Gold Fever":** Pursuing wealth to the point of foolishness.

**"Barn Money":** Savings set aside for major community project.

**"Debt Mark":** Public record of unpaid obligation.

**"Fair Weight":** Honest measurement in trade.

**"Clipped Coin":** Currency shaved for metal (fraud).

**"Spring Poor":** Having depleted reserves by winter's end.

**"Harvest Rich":** Temporary wealth after autumn selling.

**"Ice Broke":** Unable to pay debts (as in thin ice).

**"Solid Ground":** Financially stable.

**"One Winter Deep":** Having enough reserves for one winter.

**"Stone Solid":** Wealthy enough to survive multiple bad years.

---

<!-- FILE_START: ../World Building/Practical/Common_Goods_and_Services.md -->
# Common Goods and Services

{{wide
## The Economics of the Frontier

Northreach operates on a practical economy. Goods are priced based on scarcity, transport costs, and immediate usefulness. What costs coppers in Solaris might cost gold pieces here—and what seems expensive in the south might be worthless on the frontier.
}}

{{descriptive
"Everything costs more up north, except land and trouble. Those are free."

—Common saying among Northreach merchants
}}

---

## Understanding Frontier Pricing

### The Frontier Surcharge

Most manufactured goods cost **1.5× standard PHB prices** in Northreach settlements due to:
- Long supply lines from the south
- Dangerous transport routes
- Limited local production
- Seasonal scarcity (especially winter)

**Exceptions:**
- Basic rations and local produce (no surcharge)
- Services provided by locals (standard rates)
- Goods the Wardens provide to members (see Guild Benefits)

### Seasonal Price Fluctuations

**Spring (Thaw to Planting):**
- Food: Standard prices
- Healing supplies: +25% (winter depleted stocks)
- Transport: -25% (caravans resume)

**Summer (Planting to Harvest):**
- Food: -10% (fresh produce)
- All goods: Standard frontier pricing
- Transport: Widely available

**Autumn (Harvest to First Snow):**
- Food: -20% (harvest surplus)
- Winter gear: +50% (demand increases)
- Transport: +25% (last caravans)

**Winter (First Snow to Thaw):**
- Food: +50% (stored goods only)
- Healing potions: +100% (scarce, life-saving)
- Transport: Not available
- Firewood: 5× normal price

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote COMMON GOODS AND SERVICES}}

\page

## Room and Board

### Waystone Inn (Guild Headquarters)

**For Northwatch Wardens (Members Only):**
- **Lodging:** Free (bunk in common quarters)
- **Meals:** Free (hearty stew, bread, ale)
- **Stable:** Free (for mounts on guild business)
- **Basic healing:** Free (mundane treatment, Medicine checks)
- **Access to library:** Free (Lorewarden Elric's collection)

**For Non-Members:**
- **Common room:** 1 gp/night (includes meals)
- **Private room:** 5 gp/night
- **Meals only:** 3 sp (breakfast), 5 sp (dinner)
- **Stable:** 5 sp/night per animal

{{note
##### Guild Benefit

This is one of the most valuable benefits of Warden membership. A common room at any other inn costs 5 sp minimum, and meals add up quickly. Over a month, free room and board saves each Warden approximately 20-30 gp.
}}

\column

### Other Northreach Inns

**The Shepherd's Crook (Welton):**
- **Squalid:** 2 sp/night (barn loft, shared blanket)
- **Poor:** 4 sp/night (common room, thin mattress)
- **Modest:** 8 sp/night (shared room, real bed)
- **Comfortable:** 2 gp/night (private room)
- **Meals:** 3 sp (simple), 1 gp (quality)

**Snowmelt Inn (Palebank Village):**
- **Poor:** 5 sp/night
- **Modest:** 1 gp/night
- **Comfortable:** 3 gp/night (scarce)
- **Wealthy:** Not available
- **Meals:** 5 sp (fish-heavy menu)

**The Broken Wheel (Pinebrook):**
- **Poor:** 4 sp/night
- **Modest:** 8 sp/night
- **Comfortable:** 2 gp/night
- **Meals:** 4 sp (game meat common)

**Traveler's Rest (Divinity's Beacon):**
- **Modest:** 1 gp/night
- **Comfortable:** 4 gp/night
- **Wealthy:** 10 gp/night (pilgrim suites)
- **Meals:** 1 gp (temple donations expected)

{{descriptive
"The Waystone serves food meant to stick to your ribs and keep you warm. Other inns serve food meant to empty your purse."

—Willen, Hearthwarden cook at Waystone Inn
}}

{{pageNumber,auto}}

\page

## Professional Services

### Healing and Medicine

**Mundane Treatment (Medicine Checks):**
- **First aid:** 5 sp (bandaging, basic care)
- **Disease/poison treatment:** 5 gp/day (extended care, herbalism)
- **Surgery:** 25 gp (setting bones, removing arrows)
- **Failure risk:** Practitioner makes Medicine check; failure may worsen condition

**Magical Healing (Clerics/Paladins):**
- **Cure Wounds (1st):** 50 gp
- **Lesser Restoration (2nd):** 100 gp
- **Prayer of Healing (2nd):** 150 gp (multiple recipients)
- **Remove Curse (3rd):** 300 gp
- **Greater Restoration (5th):** 1,000 gp (extremely rare)

**Healing Potions:**
- **Potion of Healing:** 75 gp (scarce; limited stock)
- **Potion of Greater Healing:** 300 gp (very rare)

**Temple Services (Divinity's Beacon):**
- Basic healing spells available at 75% normal cost
- Donations expected (10% of service value minimum)
- Emergency services provided regardless of ability to pay

{{note
##### Father Merriksonn (Welton)

The local cleric in Welton provides healing at reduced rates for community members: 25 gp for Cure Wounds, 50 gp for Lesser Restoration. He expects labor or goods in trade if coin is scarce. He'll treat Wardens at these rates in exchange for guild protection of the village.
}}

\column

### Crafting and Repair

**Blacksmith Services:**
- **Weapon sharpening:** 5 sp (restores dulled weapon)
- **Armor repair (light):** 2 gp
- **Armor repair (medium):** 5 gp
- **Armor repair (heavy):** 10 gp
- **Weapon repair:** 3 gp (per broken weapon)
- **Custom work:** PHB price × 2 (frontier smith premium)
- **Smithing time:** 1 day per 50 gp value

**Leatherworker:**
- **Boot repair:** 5 sp
- **Leather armor repair:** 2 gp
- **New gear (belts, pouches):** PHB price × 1.5
- **Saddle repair:** 3 gp

**Tailor/Weaver:**
- **Clothing repair:** 1 sp
- **New common clothes:** 8 sp
- **Cold weather outfit:** 15 gp (insulated, essential for winter)
- **Fine clothes:** 25 gp (rare, special order)

**Carpenter:**
- **Wagon repair:** 5 gp/day (materials extra)
- **Building repair:** 2 gp/day (simple work)
- **Custom furniture:** 10 gp/item

**Fletcher:**
- **Arrow repair/refletching:** 1 cp per arrow
- **New arrows:** 1 gp per 20 (frontier price)
- **Specialty arrows:** 5 gp per 10 (silvered, etc.)

### Information and Investigation

**Sage/Lorewarden Elric Vael (Waystone Inn):**
- **General knowledge:** Free for Wardens

- **Arcane identification:** 25 gp (Identify equivalent)
- **Ancient texts:** 50 gp + 1d4 days research
- **Rare lore:** 100+ gp, weeks of research

**Local Informants:**
- **Rumor gathering:** 5 sp/day (tavern gossip)
- **Specific information:** 1-10 gp (depends on risk)
- **Ongoing surveillance:** 5 gp/day
- **Quality varies:** Persuasion or Deception checks may be needed

**Guides and Scouts:**
- **Local guide (settlement to settlement):** 2 gp/day
- **Wilderness guide (trackless):** 5 gp/day
- **Dangerous terrain:** 10 gp/day
- **Winter guide:** 15 gp/day (scarce)
- **Combat-capable scout:** 8 gp/day

{{note
##### Corel's Tracking Services

Corel, the Senior Trailwarden and halfling shepherd, occasionally hires out his tracking expertise: 10 gp/day plus expenses. His success rate is exceptional, but he only takes jobs that don't conflict with Warden duties.
}}

- **Witness/notary:** 5 sp
- **Contract drafting:** 5 gp
- **Translation:** 2 gp/page

**Legal Representation:**
- **Minor dispute:** 10 gp
- **Property dispute:** 25 gp
- **Criminal defense:** 50+ gp
- **Contract negotiation:** 15 gp

**Courier/Messenger:**
- **Local delivery (same settlement):** 1 sp
- **Settlement to settlement:** 1 gp/day of travel
- **Urgent message:** Double cost
- **Guaranteed delivery:** Triple cost + insurance

- Payment in advance for first week
- Bonus for successful completion (10-25% typical)
- Hazard pay for extreme danger (double rate)
- Equipment provided by employer
- Healing costs covered by employer

## Magical Items and Services

### Spell Scrolls

**Availability:** Extremely rare in Northreach. Most must be commissioned from Lorewarden Elric or acquired through adventuring.

**Commission Prices (from Elric):**
- **Cantrip scroll:** 25 gp + 1 day
- **1st-level scroll:** 50 gp + 2 days
- **2nd-level scroll:** 150 gp + 5 days
- **3rd-level scroll:** 300 gp + 1 week
- **Higher levels:** Not available in Northreach

**Requires:** Spell components (provided by client if expensive)

### Spellcasting Services

Lorewarden Elric Vael occasionally provides magical services to Wardens:

**Utility Spells (For Wardens on Contract):**
- **Identify:** 25 gp (1st level)
- **Detect Magic:** 15 gp (1st level)
- **Comprehend Languages:** 25 gp (1st level)
- **Augury:** 50 gp (2nd level)
- **Locate Object:** 75 gp (2nd level)

**Combat/Adventure Spells:**
- Generally not provided
- Emergency situations only, DM discretion

{{note
##### Elric's Research Time

Lorewarden Elric is often conducting arcane research. Commission requests may take longer than standard spellcasting service times. Plan ahead and provide advance notice for time-sensitive needs.
}}

\column

### Magic Item Purchase

**Common Magic Items:**
- **Potion of Healing:** 75 gp (limited stock)
- **Potion of Climbing:** 100 gp (rare)
- **Spell scroll (cantrip):** 50 gp (if found)

**Uncommon and Higher:**
- Not available for purchase in Northreach
- Must be found in adventures or commissioned from major cities
- Transport time from Solaris: 4-8 weeks
- Deposit required: 50% upfront
- Markup: 2-3× Dungeon Master's Guide suggested value

### Enchantment Services

**Weapon/Armor Enhancement:**
- Not available in Northreach
- Solaris or dwarven craftmasters required
- Estimated cost: 500+ gp for +1 enhancement
- Time: 2-6 months

**Item Identification:**
- **Lorewarden Elric:** 25 gp (Identify spell equivalent)
- **Mundane assessment:** 5 gp (arcana check, no guarantees)

**Curse Removal:**
- **Remove Curse spell:** 300 gp
- **Greater Restoration:** 1,000 gp
- Available only from higher-level clerics in Divinity's Beacon

{{descriptive
"You want a flaming sword? Go to Solaris. Bring gold. Lots of gold. Maybe come back in a year. Or find one in some ancient ruin and hope the curse isn't too bad."

—Lorewarden Elric Vael on magic item requests
}}

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote COMMON GOODS AND SERVICES}}

\page

## Contracts and Warden Income

### Typical Contract Rewards

The Northwatch Wardens operate on a fair-pay system. Contract values are posted on the Waystone Board.

**Minor Contracts (1-2 sessions):**
- **Investigation:** 50-100 gp total
- **Escort duty:** 75-150 gp total
- **Monster hunt (common):** 100-200 gp total
- **Recovery/retrieval:** 75-125 gp total

**Standard Contracts (3-5 sessions):**
- **Major investigation:** 200-400 gp total
- **Dangerous escort:** 300-500 gp total
- **Monster hunt (deadly):** 400-800 gp total
- **Ruin exploration:** 300-600 gp total + found treasure

**Extraordinary Contracts (6+ sessions):**
- **Regional threat:** 800-1,500 gp total
- **Major diplomatic mission:** 600-1,200 gp total
- **Deep wilderness expedition:** 1,000-2,000 gp total + salvage rights

**Payment Structure:**
- **Upfront:** 25% on contract acceptance
- **Completion:** 75% on successful resolution
- **Guild cut:** 10% goes to Warden operations (already calculated in posted rewards)
- **Split:** Divided equally among participants unless otherwise negotiated

{{note
##### Example: Wolves of Welton

Contract W-17 posted reward: 800 gp  
Party of 3 Wardens completes it  
Each Warden receives: 266 gp (guild's 10% already deducted)  
Payment on completion at Waystone Inn
}}

\column

### Additional Income Sources

**Treasure and Salvage:**
- Anything found beyond contract objectives belongs to finders
- Guild takes no cut of found treasure
- Valuable finds should be reported (information purposes)

**Crafting and Trade:**
- Wardens can sell crafted goods
- Can trade with merchants independently
- Can establish side businesses during downtime

**Services to Community:**
- Local settlements may pay for specific help
- Prices vary by need and ability to pay
- Builds reputation and goodwill

**Bounties:**
- Posted by local authorities
- Typically 50-500 gp depending on threat
- "Dead or alive" (prefer alive for questioning)

---

## Living Expenses

### Lifestyle Costs (per Week)

**Warden Members (Using Guild Benefits):**
- **Minimum:** 5 gp (personal items, incidentals)
- **Modest:** 10 gp (occasional treats, better gear)
- **Comfortable:** 25 gp (quality personal items, savings)

**Non-Members (Standard PHB Guidelines):**
- **Wretched:** 0 gp (homeless, begging)
- **Squalid:** 1 sp/day (7 sp/week)
- **Poor:** 2 sp/day (1 gp 4 sp/week)
- **Modest:** 1 gp/day (7 gp/week)
- **Comfortable:** 2 gp/day (14 gp/week)
- **Wealthy:** 4 gp/day (28 gp/week)
- **Aristocratic:** 10+ gp/day (70+ gp/week)
