## Shopping Quick Reference

### Essential Gear for New Wardens

**Minimum Equipment (If Not Using Class Starting Gear):**
- Weapon (appropriate to class): 15-75 gp
- Armor (appropriate to class): 15-75 gp
- Adventuring pack: 10-15 gp
- Waterskin: 3 sp
- Rations (10 days): 5 gp
- Bedroll: 1 gp 5 sp
- Rope (50 ft): 1 gp 5 sp
- Torches (10): 1 sp
- Tinderbox: 7 sp 5 cp
- Backpack: 3 gp

**Total Minimum:** ~75-150 gp (highly variable by class)

**Cold Weather Addition (Essential for Autumn/Winter):**
- Cold weather outfit: 15 gp
- Winter blanket: 1 gp
- Snowshoes: 2 gp

**Recommended Additions:**
- Healer's kit: 7 gp 5 sp
- Tent (if no shelter available): 3-15 gp
- Extra rations: 5 gp/10 days
- Healing potion (1): 75 gp
- Lock picks (if rogue): 37 gp 5 sp

---

### Sample Budget: First Month as a Warden

**Income:**
- 2 standard contracts completed: ~400-500 gp each
- Personal share (party of 4): ~200-250 gp total

**Expenses:**
- Lodging/food: 0 gp (guild benefit)
- Equipment repairs: 10-20 gp
- Healing (if needed): 25-100 gp
- Resupply (rations, ammunition): 10-15 gp
- Personal lifestyle: 10-40 gp
- Savings/emergency fund: 50-100 gp

**Net:** Most Wardens can save 50-150 gp per month while maintaining modest-to-comfortable lifestyle, assuming regular contracts and moderate danger.

}}

{{wide
## Merchant Price Negotiation

### Haggling in Northreach

Frontier merchants expect negotiation, but the margin is thin. Success requires both skill and respect.

**Persuasion Check Results:**

| Check Result | Price Adjustment |
|:-------------|:-----------------|
| 5 or lower | Merchant offended; +10% markup |
| 6-10 | No change; merchant holds firm |
| 11-15 | 5% discount on total purchase |
| 16-20 | 10% discount on total purchase |
| 21-25 | 15% discount + future favor |
| 26+ | 20% discount + merchant becomes contact |

**Modifiers:**
- **Bulk purchase (50+ gp):** +2 to check
- **Repeat customer:** +2 to check
- **Guild member:** +1 to check
- **Poor reputation:** -2 to check
- **Attempting to haggle necessities during winter:** -5 to check (bad form)

**Cultural Notes:**
- Haggling is expected for major purchases (weapons, armor, tools)
- Haggling for food or basic supplies is considered rude
- Never haggle with healers during emergencies
- Always haggle with merchants from Vharoxis (they expect it)

---

## Barter and Trade

### When Coin is Scarce

Northreach settlements often operate on trade and favor systems, especially in winter or after poor harvests.

**Commonly Accepted Trade Goods:**
- **Furs and pelts:** 5-50 gp value depending on quality
- **Preserved meat:** 1 gp/5 lbs
- **Medicinal herbs:** 5-20 gp per bundle
- **Crafted goods:** Varies by quality and need
- **Labor:** 2-5 sp per day worked

**Services for Trade:**
- Monster extermination
- Building repairs
- Healing services
- Protection/guarding
- Magical assistance

**Reputation as Currency:**
- Completing contracts builds trust
- Communities remember who helped them
- May receive free lodging, supplies, or information
- "You helped us during the wolf attacks; least we can do is feed you"

}}

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote COMMON GOODS AND SERVICES}}

\page

{{wide
## Special Considerations

### Seasonal Scarcity

**Items Always Available:**
- Basic food (bread, preserved rations)
- Common clothing
- Simple tools
- Firewood (expensive in winter)
- Basic weapons (axes, spears, bows)

**Items Seasonally Scarce:**
- Fresh produce (winter)
- Healing potions (winter, after major incidents)
- Complex repairs (winter - smiths focus on essential work)
- Mounts (winter - too dangerous to travel)
- Luxury goods (always scarce, worse in winter)

**Items Nearly Impossible to Find:**
- Plate armor (must commission from south)
- Magic items (except potions)
- Exotic spell components
- Fine wines and delicacies
- Books and scrolls (except Elric's library)

---

## Emergency Prices

When supplies are critically low or danger is immediate, prices skyrocket:

**Crisis Pricing (Blizzard, Siege, Disaster):**
- Basic rations: 5× normal
- Healing: 3× normal
- Firewood: 10× normal
- Shelter: 5× normal
- Ammunition: 3× normal

**Price Gouging:**
- Considered deeply dishonorable in Northreach
- Communities remember and shun those who exploit crises
- Wardens investigate and may intervene
- Marshal Brenna has been known to "requisition" hoarded supplies during emergencies

{{descriptive
"There's making a profit, and then there's robbing people when they're desperate. The first is business. The second gets you run out of town—if you're lucky."

—Steward Mara Fenwick on merchant ethics
}}

}}

{{footnote COMMON GOODS AND SERVICES}}

\page

# Travel and Distance in Northreach

{{wide
## Journey Planning for the Frontier

The frontier rewards preparation and punishes haste. Understanding travel times, seasonal conditions, and the costs of movement can mean the difference between a successful contract and a frozen corpse on the roadside.
}}

{{descriptive
"Three days to Palebank in summer. Five in autumn mud. Seven in winter snow—if you're lucky and the wolves stay hungry somewhere else."

—Corel, Senior Trailwarden
}}

---

## Travel Times from Waystone Inn

### Major Settlements

The following times assume **good weather, daylight travel, and a party on foot** with standard equipment. Mounted travel or wagons will vary (see Travel Methods below).

{{wide

| Destination | Distance | On Foot | Mounted | Wagon | Notable Hazards |
|:------------|:---------|:--------|:--------|:------|:----------------|
| **Welton** | ~25 miles | 1 day | 1 day | 2 days | Wolves (frequent) |
| **Palebank Village** | ~70 miles | 3 days | 2 days | 5 days | Ice frogs, winter weather |
| **Pinebrook** | ~45 miles | 2 days | 1 day | 3 days | Trolls (rare), bandits |
| **Noke's Tower** | ~18 miles | 1 day | 1 day | 1 day | Magical anomalies |
| **Divinity's Beacon** | ~90 miles | 4 days | 3 days | 6 days | Rugged terrain, pilgrims |
| **The Far North** | ~200+ miles | 9+ days | 6+ days | Impassable | Everything |

}}

{{note
##### Quick Reference: One Day's Travel

**On Foot:** 24 miles (open terrain), 18 miles (forest), 12 miles (mountains)  
**Mounted:** 30 miles (open), 24 miles (forest), 18 miles (rough terrain)  
**Wagon:** 15 miles (roads only), impassable in mountains or deep forest
}}

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote TRAVEL AND DISTANCE IN NORTHREACH}}

\page

### Settlement-to-Settlement Routes

Common routes between Northreach settlements:

**Welton to Palebank Village**
- Distance: ~50 miles northeast
- Time: 2 days on foot, 1.5 days mounted
- Route: North road through pine forests, coastal approach
- Hazards: Coastal storms, ice during winter

**Welton to Pinebrook**
- Distance: ~35 miles west
- Time: 1.5 days on foot, 1 day mounted
- Route: Western forest road
- Hazards: Dense forest, occasional troll sightings

**Palebank to Salsvault** (Far North ruins)
- Distance: ~130 miles north
- Time: 6 days on foot minimum, 4 days mounted
- Route: No established roads; wilderness navigation
- Hazards: Extreme cold, dire wolves, ice elementals, isolation
- **Special:** Requires Survival DC 15 checks daily, cold weather gear mandatory

{{note
##### Chartering Transport

**Wagon hire:** 5 gp/day + driver (2 gp/day)  
**Horse rental:** 3 gp/day (8 gp/day for warhorse)  
**Guide/Scout:** 2 gp/day  
**Armed escort:** 5 gp/day per guard

Steward Mara Fenwick can arrange transport for official Warden contracts.
}}

\column

## Travel Methods

### On Foot (Standard)

Most Wardens travel on foot—it's reliable, doesn't require feed, and allows for investigation along the route.

**Speeds by Terrain:**
- **Open Terrain** (roads, plains): 24 miles/day
- **Light Forest** (maintained trails): 18 miles/day
- **Dense Forest** (game trails): 12 miles/day
- **Mountains** (rugged paths): 12 miles/day
- **Swamp or Deep Snow**: 6 miles/day

**Carrying Capacity:** Standard PHB rules apply. Characters with 15+ Strength can maintain normal speed while carrying heavy loads; those with lower Strength should plan accordingly.

**Forced March:** Traveling more than 8 hours requires a Constitution saving throw (DC 10 + 1 per hour beyond 8) or gain one level of exhaustion.

### Mounted Travel

Horses are expensive to maintain on the frontier but offer significant advantages.

**Riding Horse:**
- Speed: 30 miles/day (open), 24 miles/day (light forest)
- Cost: 75 gp to purchase, 3 gp/day to rent
- Feed: 5 sp/day (stable), forage possible in summer (Survival DC 12)
- Cannot navigate mountains or deep forest effectively

**Draft Horse (Wagon):**
- Speed: 15 miles/day on roads only
- Capacity: 540 lbs or 6 people
- Cost: 50 gp to purchase, 5 gp/day to rent with wagon
- Feed: 5 sp/day
- Roads required; impassable in rough terrain

**Warhorse:**
- Speed: Same as riding horse
- Combat-trained (doesn't panic)
- Cost: 400 gp to purchase, 8 gp/day to rent
- Rare in Northreach; usually owned by nobles or wealthy mercenaries

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote TRAVEL AND DISTANCE IN NORTHREACH}}

\page

### Snowshoes and Winter Travel

Winter travel in Northreach requires specialized equipment.

**Snowshoes:**
- Cost: 2 gp
- Effect: Negates difficult terrain from snow (up to 2 feet deep)
- Speed: Normal walking speed in snow
- Without snowshoes: Snow counts as difficult terrain (half speed)

**Sleds:**
- Cost: 10 gp (small), 25 gp (large)
- Capacity: 300 lbs (small), 800 lbs (large)
- Requires 1 person (small) or 2 people + draft animal (large)
- Speed: 12 miles/day in snow

---

## Seasonal Conditions

Northreach's harsh seasons dramatically affect travel. Plan accordingly or risk death.

### Spring (Thaw Moon to Planting Moon)

**Conditions:** Muddy roads, swollen rivers, unpredictable weather  
**Temperature:** 35-55°F during day, freezing at night  
**Travel Impact:** Roads become difficult terrain; river crossings dangerous

**Effects:**
- Wagon travel reduced by 50% (mud)
- Athletics checks (DC 12) to cross swollen streams
- Random spring storms (10% chance/day)

**Advantages:**
- Game returns; foraging becomes possible (Survival DC 12)
- Fewer predators (many still denning)

\column

### Summer (Planting Moon to Harvest Moon)

**Conditions:** Mild, wet, occasionally hot  
**Temperature:** 55-75°F, rare nights below 45°F  
**Travel Impact:** Best season for travel

**Effects:**
- Normal travel speeds
- No cold weather survival checks
- Foraging easy (Survival DC 10)

**Challenges:**
- Insects (mostly annoyance)
- Thunderstorms (15% chance/day in late summer)
- Increased bandit activity on roads

{{note
##### Summer Travel Advantage

This is the only season where inexperienced travelers can reasonably survive Northreach roads. Most merchant caravans operate exclusively in summer months.
}}

### Autumn (Harvest Moon to First Snow)

**Conditions:** Cool, increasingly unpredictable, early snow possible  
**Temperature:** 40-60°F early autumn, 25-45°F late autumn  
**Travel Impact:** Deteriorating conditions; race against winter

**Effects:**
- Early autumn: Normal travel
- Late autumn (after first frost): Travel speeds reduced 25%
- Constitution saves (DC 10) for extended outdoor exposure in late autumn

**Challenges:**
- Weather changes rapidly
- Game migrates; foraging becomes difficult (Survival DC 15)
- Communities stockpiling; hospitality strained

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote TRAVEL AND DISTANCE IN NORTHREACH}}

\page

### Winter (First Snow to Thaw Moon)

**Conditions:** Lethal cold, deep snow, blizzards  
**Temperature:** -10°F to 30°F, windchill often -20°F or lower  
**Travel Impact:** Extremely dangerous; avoid unless absolutely necessary

{{descriptive
"Winter doesn't care about your courage, your mission, or your god. It just kills. Respect it or join the frozen."

—Marshal Brenna Thorne
}}

**Survival Requirements:**

**Cold Weather Outfit** (mandatory)
- Cost: 10 gp
- Effect: Grants advantage on Constitution saves against cold
- Without it: Automatic failure on survival checks

**Shelter** (required nightly)
- Tent/lean-to: Constitution save DC 10 to avoid exhaustion
- Building with fire: No save required
- No shelter: Constitution save DC 15 to avoid exhaustion, disadvantage without cold weather outfit

**Daily Survival Checks:**
Traveling in winter requires a Constitution saving throw at the end of each day:
- **DC 10** with shelter and fire
- **DC 15** with shelter, no fire
- **DC 20** without shelter (automatic failure without cold weather outfit)

**Failure:** Gain one level of exhaustion

**Snowstorm Survival:**
During blizzards (20% chance per winter day):
- Visibility reduced to 30 feet
- All terrain is difficult terrain
- Constitution save DC 18 to avoid exhaustion
- Impossible to forage or hunt
- High risk of getting lost (Survival DC 18 to navigate)

\column

**Winter Travel Speeds:**
- Snow depth 1-2 feet: Half speed (snowshoes negate)
- Snow depth 3+ feet: Quarter speed (snowshoes reduce to half speed)
- During blizzard: Travel not recommended

{{note
##### Winter Death Toll

Every winter, 10-20 travelers die on Northreach roads. Locals know: if you can delay until spring, do so. If you cannot, travel with experienced guides, bring twice the supplies you think you need, and write your will before you leave.
}}

**Winter Equipment Checklist:**
- ✓ Cold weather outfit (10 gp)
- ✓ Snowshoes (2 gp)
- ✓ Winter tent or bedroll rated for cold (25 gp)
- ✓ Tinderbox and extra kindling (2 gp)
- ✓ Double rations (assume storms delay travel)
- ✓ Healing potions (frostbite and injury common)

---

## Navigation and Getting Lost

### Staying on Course

Travel on established roads rarely requires navigation checks. Wilderness travel is another matter.

**Navigation Check (Survival):**
- **Well-Marked Trail:** No check required
- **Game Trail or Rough Direction:** DC 10
- **Trackless Wilderness:** DC 15
- **Poor Visibility (fog, storm, night):** DC 20

**Failure:** Party travels in wrong direction for 1d6 hours before realizing error. This can add hours or days to journey time.

**Tools:**
- **Navigator's Tools:** Grants advantage on navigation checks
- **Compass:** +2 to navigation checks
- **Accurate Map:** +2 to navigation checks (DM discretion on map quality)

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote TRAVEL AND DISTANCE IN NORTHREACH}}

\page

### Landmarks and Wayfinding

Experienced travelers use natural and artificial landmarks:

**Natural Landmarks:**
- **North Star (clear nights):** Provides automatic directional sense
- **Moss growth:** Unreliable (DC 20 Survival to use effectively)
- **Prevailing winds:** DC 15 Survival to interpret
- **Animal trails:** Often lead to water, but not always to safety

**Artificial Landmarks:**
- **Cairns (stone markers):** Indicate traveled routes
- **Blazed trees:** Trail markers cut into bark
- **Road stones:** Placed every mile on major roads
- **Distant smoke:** Settlements or camps (investigate cautiously)

{{note
##### Lorewarden's Library Maps

The Waystone Inn maintains maps of known routes and dangers. Wardens can copy these maps before departing (1 hour work, cartographer's tools). Lorewarden Elric Vael personally updates them based on field reports.
}}

---

## Terrain Types and Hazards

### Open Terrain (Plains, Roads)

**Travel Speed:** 24 miles/day on foot, 30 miles/day mounted  
**Navigation:** Easy (DC 10 or no check on roads)  
**Cover:** Minimal; difficult to hide or ambush  
**Hazards:** Exposure to weather, visible to threats from distance

**Recommended For:** Rapid travel between settlements, wagon transport

\column

### Forest (Light)

**Travel Speed:** 18 miles/day on foot, 24 miles/day mounted  
**Navigation:** Moderate (DC 12)  
**Cover:** Good for stealth and ambush  
**Hazards:** Wild animals, bandits, limited visibility

**Recommended For:** Avoiding attention, hunting, foraging

### Forest (Dense)

**Travel Speed:** 12 miles/day on foot, mounted not recommended  
**Navigation:** Difficult (DC 15)  
**Cover:** Excellent but limits movement  
**Hazards:** Disorientation, predators, difficult to get help

**Avoid Unless:** Investigating specific locations, tracking quarry, hiding from pursuit

### Mountains

**Travel Speed:** 12 miles/day on foot, mounted very difficult  
**Navigation:** Difficult (DC 15-20)  
**Cover:** Varies; exposure on ridges, shelter in valleys  
**Hazards:** Cliffs, rockslides, altitude, extreme weather, limited resources

**Special Considerations:**
- Climbing may be required (Athletics checks)
- Cold weather even in summer at high altitude
- Thin air above 10,000 feet (Constitution saves DC 12 or exhaustion)

{{note
##### Mountain Travel

Only attempt mountain crossings with experienced guides, proper equipment, and compelling reasons. The Temple of the Dragonknights expeditions lost 30% of participants to mountain hazards before even reaching the temple.
}}

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote TRAVEL AND DISTANCE IN NORTHREACH}}

\page

### Coastal Regions

**Travel Speed:** 18-24 miles/day depending on terrain  
**Navigation:** Moderate (DC 12), coastline provides orientation  
**Cover:** Minimal on beaches, good in coastal cliffs  
**Hazards:** Tides, storms, rocky shores, sea creatures

**Special Rules:**
- **Tide tracking:** High tide can cut off beach routes (Nature DC 12 to predict)
- **Storms:** Coastal storms arrive with little warning (10% chance/day, higher in autumn)
- **Cliff climbing:** Often required for coastal exploration (Athletics DC 13-18)

---

## Random Encounters

Travel in Northreach is rarely uneventful. The frequency of encounters depends on terrain and season.

### Encounter Frequency by Terrain

**Roads near settlements:** 10% chance per day  
**Wilderness trails:** 25% chance per day  
**Trackless wilderness:** 40% chance per day  
**Winter travel:** 50% chance per day (weather and creatures)

**Encounter Distance:**
- **Open terrain:** Spotted at 200-500 feet
- **Forest:** Spotted at 50-100 feet
- **Mountains:** Highly variable (50-300 feet)
- **Night or poor visibility:** 30 feet

{{note
##### DM's Note

Your DM determines actual encounter frequency and content. These percentages provide guidelines for wilderness travel pacing. Not all encounters are hostile—some may be other travelers, merchant caravans, or wandering NPCs with information.
}}

\column

### Common Encounter Types

**Wildlife (40% of encounters):**
- Wolves (most common)
- Bears (autumn, near dens)
- Owlbears (rare but deadly)
- Elk or deer (usually flee)

**Humanoids (30% of encounters):**
- Other Wardens or travelers
- Hunters and trappers
- Bandits (summer months)
- Refugees or displaced persons

**Environmental (20% of encounters):**
- Severe weather
- Difficult terrain (river crossings, cliffs)
- Natural hazards (avalanche, rockslide)
- Foraging opportunities

**Magical/Unusual (10% of encounters):**
- Awakened creatures (post-Echo)
- Strange phenomena
- Ancient ruins or landmarks
- Arcane disturbances

---

## Resting During Travel

### Short Rest (1 hour)

Can be taken during normal travel day without extending journey time. Most parties rest at midday.

**Suitable Locations:**
- Roadside clearings
- Established campsites
- Forest groves
- Sheltered valleys

**Activities During Short Rest:**
- Eating and drinking
- Tending wounds (Medicine checks)
- Repairing equipment
- Consulting maps

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote TRAVEL AND DISTANCE IN NORTHREACH}}

\page

### Long Rest (8 hours)

Requires safe location and time. Extends travel day significantly.

**Camp Setup:**
- **Time Required:** 30 minutes to establish camp, 30 minutes to break camp
- **Watch Rotation:** 2-hour shifts for parties of 4 (each gets 6 hours sleep + 2 hours watch)
- **Fire:** Provides warmth, light, and cooking but may attract attention

**Suitable Camp Locations:**

**Good Camps (Long Rest succeeds automatically):**
- Wayfarer shelters (stone huts along major roads)
- Abandoned buildings (if safe)
- Deep forest groves (concealed)
- Mountain caves (checked for occupants)

**Poor Camps (Constitution DC 10 or gain exhaustion):**
- Exposed roadside
- Wet or marshy ground
- Windy hilltops
- Areas with recent predator signs

**Dangerous Camps (Constitution DC 15 or gain exhaustion):**
- No shelter during storm
- Extremely cold without fire
- Haunted or corrupted locations
- Active monster territory

{{note
##### Wayfarer Shelters

Stone shelters exist along major Northreach roads, spaced roughly one day's travel apart. These simple structures provide protection from weather and are maintained by local communities. Always check for occupants (human or otherwise) before settling in.
}}

\column

### Watch Duty

Someone must watch for danger during long rests in the wilderness.

**Watch Rotation (4-person party):**
- 1st Watch (dusk): 2 hours
- 2nd Watch (early night): 2 hours
- 3rd Watch (midnight): 2 hours
- 4th Watch (pre-dawn): 2 hours

**Watch Duties:**
- Perception checks to detect threats (DC varies)
- Maintain fire if present
- Wake party if danger approaches
- Note unusual sounds or sights

**Sleeping in Armor:**
- Light armor: No penalty
- Medium armor: No Long Rest benefit (counts as Light Activity)
- Heavy armor: Cannot gain Long Rest benefits

{{descriptive
"First watch is when you're fresh and alert. Second watch is when you're fighting sleep. Third watch is when you think you hear everything. Fourth watch—that's when things actually happen. Stay sharp on fourth."

—Bordel Barleywind, veteran Trailwarden
}}

---

## Foraging and Hunting

Feeding a party on the road reduces supply costs but takes time and skill.

### Foraging for Food

**Time Required:** 1 hour (conducted during travel, slows party by 1 hour)  
**Skill Check:** Survival  
**DC by Season:**
- Spring: DC 14 (scarce, new growth)
- Summer: DC 10 (abundant)
- Autumn: DC 12 (harvest but dwindling)
- Winter: DC 20 (nearly impossible)

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote TRAVEL AND DISTANCE IN NORTHREACH}}

\page

**Success:** Find 1d6 pounds of edible plants, berries, roots, or mushrooms (1 pound = 1 day's food for one person)

**Terrain Modifiers:**
- Forest: +0
- Plains/Open: +2 to DC
- Mountains: +5 to DC
- Coastal: -2 to DC (shellfish, seaweed)

{{note
##### Herbalism Kit

Characters with herbalism kit proficiency can attempt to find medicinal plants while foraging. Separate Survival check (DC 15) yields 1d4 herbs suitable for crafting healing supplies.
}}

### Hunting

**Time Required:** 4 hours minimum (half-day activity)  
**Skill Check:** Survival (tracking) then attack rolls (combat)  
**DC by Season:**
- Spring/Summer: DC 12 (game abundant)
- Autumn: DC 10 (game fattening for winter)
- Winter: DC 18 (scarce, desperate)

**Success:** Encounter game appropriate to terrain
- **Rabbits/Small Game:** 1d4 pounds meat
- **Deer/Medium Game:** 3d6 pounds meat
- **Elk/Large Game:** 6d6 pounds meat

**Processing Game:**
- Requires 1 hour + Survival check DC 10
- Failure wastes 50% of meat
- Success preserves all meat
- Preserved meat lasts 1 week in cool weather, 3 days in warm weather

**Hunting Risks:**
- Attracts predators (scent of blood)
- Loud (gunshots or combat alert nearby creatures)
- Time-consuming (party must stop for hours)

\column

---

## Special Travel Situations

### Stealth Travel

When avoiding detection is critical:

**Group Stealth Check:**
- Entire party rolls Stealth
- Use slowest result
- Move at half normal speed
- Disadvantage in open terrain
- Advantage in dense forest

**Light Discipline:**
- No fires or lanterns
- Darkvision characters lead
- Humans/others navigate by starlight (Survival DC 15)

### Forced March

Traveling more than 8 hours per day:

**Each hour beyond 8:**
- Constitution save DC 10 + 1 per extra hour
- Failure: Gain one level of exhaustion
- Must Long Rest to attempt again

**Example:**
10-hour day = Con save DC 12  
12-hour day = Con save DC 14

### Traveling at Night

**Risks:**
- Cannot navigate without light (Survival DC 20)
- Encounter chance doubles
- Moving at night risks injury (Dexterity save DC 12 on rough terrain or take 1d6 damage from falls)

**Benefits:**
- Avoid daytime patrols or detection
- Cooler temperatures in summer
- Surprise sleeping creatures

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote TRAVEL AND DISTANCE IN NORTHREACH}}

\page

# Appendix

<!-- FILE_START: ../World Building/Appendix/Glossary.md -->
# Glossary of Aevoria

*A quick reference guide to terms, places, organizations, and people of the world*

---

This glossary provides pronunciation guides and brief definitions for important names, places, and concepts in Aevoria. For more detailed information, see the referenced chapters.

**Pronunciation Key:**
- Capitals indicate stressed syllables
- Phonetic spellings use common English sounds
- Regional variations noted where significant

:::

## A

**Aeor** (AY-or)
Ancient civilization of powerful mages that fell in a cataclysm. Ruins of Aeor lie buried in the Far North, and Aeorian artifacts occasionally surface. Known for ambitious arcane experiments and magical hubris. *See: The Far North, Salsvault*

**Aeorian Echo**
Phenomenon of rising magical energy emanating from buried Aeorian ruins, particularly Salsvault. Causes unpredictable magical effects, awakening intelligence in creatures, and destabilizing arcane workings. Central mystery of the Northwatch Wardens campaign. *See: Frozen Sick adventure*

**Aevoria** (ay-VOR-ee-uh)
The continent and world in which the Northwatch Wardens campaign takes place. Divided into ten major regions with diverse cultures, climates, and peoples.

**Archivists of Aeor**
Scholarly organization dedicated to studying Aeorian ruins and recovering lost knowledge safely and responsibly. Based primarily in northern research stations. Viewed with a mix of respect and caution—their work is valuable but dangerous. *See: Organizations chapter*

**Argyle** (AR-gyle)
*Common pronunciation mistake: "ar-GYE-luh"*
Settlement in the Far North. Minor frontier post dealing with harsh arctic conditions.

**Aurixean Valignaak** (or-IK-see-an VAL-ig-nahk)
*Dragon name. Common mistake: "OR-ex-ee-an"*
Silver dragon scholar and Northwatch Warden. Curious, methodical, and somewhat awkward in social situations. Specializes in investigation and historical research. Based at Waystone Inn. *See: People of Northreach chapter*

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA}}

\page

## B

**Baleth Cindermoon**
Half-elf Warden from the Emberlands. Quiet, pragmatic survivor with deep knowledge of disaster relief and improvised solutions. Carries scars from the Emberlands' destruction. Based at Waystone Inn. *See: People of Northreach chapter*

**Bordel Barleywind**
Halfling chef and keeper of Waystone Inn. Jovial, welcoming, and observant. Provides comfort food, local gossip, and practical wisdom. The Inn's emotional heart. *See: People of Northreach chapter*

**Brenna Thorne**
Marshal of the Northwatch Wardens. Human fighter from Northreach. Direct, practical leader with military background. Commands field operations and makes tactical decisions. "Work smarter, not just harder." *See: People of Northreach chapter, Northwatch Wardens chapter*

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA}}

\page

## C

**Cloakwood**
Forest region in Northreach. Dense woodland home to rangers, druids, and occasional dangerous creatures. Trade route passes through its edge.

**Corel**
Wood elf ranger-druid hybrid working with the Northwatch Wardens. Speaks little, prefers action. Expert tracker and wilderness guide. Based at Waystone Inn. *See: People of Northreach chapter*

**Covenant of the Silent Vigil**
Religious order dedicated to protecting society from unaccountable magical power. Opposes reckless arcane experimentation, demonic pacts, and dangerous artifacts. Not anti-magic, but pro-responsibility. Views vary by region—respected enforcers or zealous opposition. *See: Organizations chapter, Gods and Religion chapter*

**Croaker Cave**
Bandit hideout north of Palebank Village. Named for the croaking sounds echoing from within (frogs, not bandits). Site of conflict during Frozen Sick adventure. *See: The Frozen Sick adventure*

**Currency**
Aevoria uses standard D&D coinage: copper pieces (cp), silver pieces (sp), gold pieces (gp), and platinum pieces (pp). Regional currencies exist but are easily exchanged. *See: Currency and Trade chapter*

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA}}

\page

## D

**Divinity's Beacon** (div-IN-ih-tees BEE-kun)
Holy city in the heartlands of the Solaris Dominion. Multi-faith center of pilgrimage and theological study. Neutral ground for all faiths. Home to grand temples, libraries, and religious scholars. Known for hospitality to pilgrims and fierce opposition to unaccountable magic. *See: Places of Legend chapter*

**Dragonknights, The**
Cult of dragon-worshippers who sought to gain draconic power through rituals and pacts. Led by Brother Alastair. Believed dragons were superior beings deserving worship and service. Defeated in the Temple of the Dragonknights adventure. *See: Temple of the Dragonknights adventure*

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA}}

\page

## E

**Eclipse Day**
Historical event in Solaris. Natural solar eclipse that occurred during a major cultural moment. Commemorated with silence and reflection. Specific details vary by telling. *See: Solaris Dominion chapter*

**Elric Vael** (EL-rik VAYL)
Lorewarden of the Northwatch Wardens. Half-elf scholar and divination wizard. Provides research support, arcane expertise, and historical context. Curious, methodical, slightly absent-minded. "The answer is in the archives." *See: People of Northreach chapter, Northwatch Wardens chapter*

**Elro Aldataur** (EL-roh al-DAH-tor)
*Common mistake: "el-ROH al-duh-TAR"*
Elf scholar in Palebank Village. Researches Aeorian history and the source of the mysterious illness. Knowledgeable but somewhat reckless in pursuit of discovery. *See: People of Northreach chapter, Frozen Sick adventure*

**Emberlands**
Region of Aevoria devastated by magical cataclysm within living memory. Landscape torn by lingering fire and earth magic. Home to resilient survivors, the Red Covenant disaster relief organization, and desperate communities. Known for improvisation and fierce determination. *See: Regions chapter*

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA}}

\page

## F

**Far North, The**
Arctic region at the top of the world. Home to buried Aeorian ruins, extreme weather, and isolated settlements. Inhabited by hardy folk, nomadic tribes, and researchers studying Aeor. Source of the Aeorian Echo phenomenon. *See: Regions chapter*

**Father Johan Merriksonn** (YOH-han MEH-rik-sun)
*"Father Johan" is fine; full name rarely used*
Dwarf cleric of the Stonefather in Northreach. Provides healing, spiritual guidance, and community support. Practical faith focused on endurance and honest work. Based in a modest shrine near Waystone Inn. *See: People of Northreach chapter*

**Finethir Shinebright** (FIN-uh-theer SHINE-bright)
*Sheep polymorphed into human form*
Polymorphed sheep seeking help to stop his polymorphing wizard brother Noke. Panicked, confused, and desperate. Central character in The Wild Sheep Chase adventure. *See: Wild Sheep Chase adventure*

**First Settlers, The**
Historical group that established Northreach settlements generations ago. Arrived from various southern regions seeking opportunity and freedom. Their stories and traditions form the foundation of Northreach culture. *See: Northreach chapter, Songs of Northreach*

**Freelance Brotherhood**
Loose network of independent adventurers, mercenaries, and problem-solvers. Not a formal organization—more of a mutual aid society. Helps members find work, share information, and avoid dangerous contracts. Viewed as pragmatic professionals or unreliable freelancers depending on perspective. *See: Organizations chapter*

**Frozen Sick**
Mysterious illness affecting Palebank Village. Victims develop icy blue veins, fever despite cold skin, and eventual crystallization. Caused by exposure to Aeorian spores from Salsvault. Curable with frigid woe antidote. *See: Frozen Sick adventure*

**Flynt Wymblen**
Gnome tinkerer and inventor working with the Northwatch Wardens. Enthusiastic gadgeteer with variable success rate. Provides experimental equipment and creative solutions (with occasional explosions). Based at Waystone Inn. *See: People of Northreach chapter*

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA}}

\page

## G

**Galvena Aballon** (gal-VEE-nah ah-BAL-on)
*Common mistake: "gal-VEN-uh"*
Human ex-soldier recruited to the Northwatch Wardens. Disciplined, loyal, struggles with nightmares from past battles. Competent warrior seeking new purpose. Based at Waystone Inn. *See: People of Northreach chapter*

**Gleaners, The**
Rural mutual aid network in farming regions. Help neighbors with harvests, barn-raisings, and recovery from disasters. Informal but reliable. Represent community values of shared labor. *See: Organizations chapter*

**Guz**
Half-orc laborer and Northwatch Warden. Quiet, immensely strong, kind-hearted. Does heavy lifting and manual work. Often underestimated due to his silence. Excellent judge of character. Based at Waystone Inn. *See: People of Northreach chapter, Songs of Northreach*

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA}}

\page

## H

**Horizon Wayfinders**
Organization of scouts, cartographers, and guides specializing in frontier exploration. Reliable sources for maps, route information, and frontier intelligence. Neutral and professional. *See: Organizations chapter*

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA}}

## I

*No major entries*

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA}}

## J

**Joel Andersmith**
Human blacksmith in Northreach settlements. Practical craftsman providing weapon repair, horseshoes, and general metalwork. Reliable, straightforward, charges fair prices. *See: People of Northreach chapter*

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA}}

\page

## K

**Khardûn-Tharum** (kar-DOON THAR-um)
*Dwarven name. Stress first and third syllables.*
Capital city of the Stonebound Depths. Great underground metropolis carved into living stone. Center of dwarven craft, culture, and geomancy. Known for resonance halls and ancestral vaults. *See: Stonebound Depths chapter*

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA}}

\page

## L

**Leanor Slatebeard** (LEE-nor SLAYT-beerd)
Dwarf tracker in Welton. Gruff, pragmatic, expert at reading wilderness signs. Helps investigate wolf attacks on Westly's farm. Takes contracts but cares about community safety. *See: People of Northreach chapter, Wolves of Welton adventure*

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA}}

\page

## M

**Mara Fenwick**
Steward of the Northwatch Wardens. Human quartermaster from merchant family background. Manages supplies, logistics, and finances with cheerful efficiency. "We'll make it work." *See: People of Northreach chapter, Northwatch Wardens chapter*

**Mila Teno** (MY-luh TEH-noh)
*Common mistake: "mee-LAH"*
Human cartographer and clerk for the Northwatch Wardens. Organized, detail-focused, maintains mission records and maps. Provides intelligence and documentation support. Based at Waystone Inn. *See: People of Northreach chapter*

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA}}

\page

## N

**Noke** (NOHK)
*Rhymes with "spoke"*
Polymorphing wizard conducting dangerous experiments. Finethir's brother. Accidentally transformed himself into a sheep and is pursued in the Wild Sheep Chase adventure. Ambitious researcher with poor judgment. *See: Wild Sheep Chase adventure*

**Noke's Tower**
Wizard's tower west of Waystone Inn. Site of Noke's polymorphing experiments. Contains spell components, research notes, magical traps, and aggressive sheep. *See: Wild Sheep Chase adventure*

**Northreach**
Frontier region of Aevoria. The player characters' starting location. Characterized by harsh winters, practical communities, and frontier independence. Home to the Waystone Inn (Northwatch Wardens headquarters). Known for resilience, hospitality to newcomers, and deep suspicion of authority. *See: Northreach chapter*

**Northwatch Wardens**
Adventuring guild based at Waystone Inn in Northreach. Operates on contract system—members take jobs and get paid. Leadership triad: Marshal Brenna Thorne (tactics), Steward Mara Fenwick (logistics), Lorewarden Elric Vael (research). Motto: "We watch. We act. We endure." *See: Northwatch Wardens chapter*

**Nullwood Expanse** (NULL-wood ex-PANS)
Elven-dominated forest region characterized by silence wards and memory preservation culture. Home to the Silent Court. Trees absorb sound; inhabitants speak in whispers and gestures. Values memory, records, and cautious change. *See: Regions chapter*

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA}}

## O

*No major entries*

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA}}

\page

## P

**Palebank Village**
Coastal settlement in northeast Northreach. Fishing and trade community near frozen wilderness. Site of the Frozen Sick adventure where mysterious illness strikes. Gateway to northern exploration. *See: Northreach chapter, Frozen Sick adventure*

**Pelc** (PELK)
*Rhymes with "elk"*
Human merchant in Palebank Village. Trades in furs, fish, and expedition supplies. Practical, profit-minded but fair. Source of local information and goods. *See: People of Northreach chapter*

**Pinebrook**
Trading village in southeast Northreach. Agricultural and commerce focus. Site of "Peril in Pinebrook" adventure involving mysterious disappearances. *See: Northreach chapter, Peril in Pinebrook adventure*

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA}}

## Q

*No major entries*

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA}}

\page

## R

**Red Covenant, The**
Disaster relief organization operating in the Emberlands and beyond. Provides aid, rebuilding assistance, and refugee support. Funded by donations and wealthy patrons. Viewed with deep respect—they work where others won't. *See: Organizations chapter*

**Resonance**
Dwarven cultural practice of listening to stone. Geomantic technique for understanding structural integrity, finding ore, and detecting danger. Both practical skill and spiritual connection to the Stonefather. *See: Stonebound Depths chapter*

**Rowan Fairweather**
Human bard and Northwatch Warden. Charismatic storyteller, morale booster, and negotiator. Performs at Waystone Inn, gathers rumors, handles diplomatic situations. "There's always a story here." Based at Waystone Inn. *See: People of Northreach chapter*

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA}}

\page

## S

**Salsvault** (SALZ-volt)
*Stress first syllable*
Buried Aeorian ruin far north of Palebank Village. Source of frigid woe spores and the Aeorian Echo phenomenon. Dangerous research site containing ancient magical experiments. *See: Frozen Sick adventure, The Far North chapter*

**Sera Gelanadel** (SAIR-uh gel-AN-uh-del)
*Elven name. Common mistake: "suh-RAH"*
High elf sorcerer and Northwatch Warden. Noble background, arcane expertise, diplomatic skills. Handles magical investigations and social situations. Polished but genuine. Based at Waystone Inn. *See: People of Northreach chapter*

**Shepherd's Crook Inn**
Community gathering place in Welton. Local tavern and social hub run by welcoming proprietors. Source of village news and gossip. *See: Welton, Wolves of Welton adventure*

**Silent Court, The**
Governing body of the Nullwood Expanse. Elven council that preserves memory and protects the forest. Deliberate, cautious, values tradition. Communicates in elaborate sign language and whispers. Distrusts rapid change and outsiders. *See: Organizations chapter, Nullwood Expanse chapter*

**Solace Nexus** (SOH-luss NEX-us)
Ley-line port city in the Verdant Marches. Hub for regulated magical transportation and spellwork. Known for arcane bureaucracy, spell licensing, and magical trade. Efficient but paperwork-heavy. *See: Places of Legend chapter*

**Solaris** (soh-LAIR-iss)
*Region and city share the name*
Cultural capital of Aevoria and the Solaris Dominion. Center of arts, politics, bardic colleges, and courtly intrigue. Known for Eclipse Day commemoration, sophisticated culture, and complex social politics. *See: Regions chapter*

**Solaris Dominion**
Southern region of Aevoria centered on the city of Solaris. Characterized by cultural sophistication, strong Radiant Queen worship, and political complexity. Heartland of civilization and traditional power structures. *See: Regions chapter*

**Solace Trade Consortium**
Powerful merchant guild controlling most long-distance trade routes. Provides banking, contract enforcement, and trade negotiations. Essential for commerce but expensive. Viewed as reliable professionals or greedy monopolists depending on perspective. *See: Organizations chapter*

**Stonebound Assembly**
Governing council of the Stonebound Depths. Dwarven leadership based on clan representation and demonstrated craft mastery. Values tradition, quality work, and community stability. *See: Organizations chapter, Stonebound Depths chapter*

**Stonebound Depths**
Dwarven homeland beneath southern mountains. Underground realm of mines, forges, and great halls. Known for masterwork crafting, ancestral traditions, resonance geomancy, and stone expertise. Values endurance, quality, and honoring ancestors. *See: Regions chapter*

**Stonefather, The**
Dwarven deity of craft, endurance, and stone. Patron of artisans, miners, and those who build things to last. Emphasis on honest work and practical faith. *See: Gods and Religion chapter*

**Sunken Dominion**
Underwater realm of aquatic peoples (merfolk, tritons, sea elves). Explored through diving, water-breathing magic, or coastal settlements with mixed population. Known for beautiful coral architecture and mysterious deep-sea cultures. *See: Regions chapter*

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA}}

\page

## T

**Takk Oaksplitter** (TAK OAK-split-er)
*"Takk" rhymes with "back"*
Half-orc carpenter and Northwatch Warden. Skilled woodworker providing construction, repairs, and carpentry. Calm, methodical, takes pride in quality work. Based at Waystone Inn. *See: People of Northreach chapter*

**Temple of the Dragonknights**
Cult stronghold in the northwest mountains of Northreach. Site of dragon-worshipping rituals and draconic power experiments. Location of capstone adventure for Season One. *See: Temple of the Dragonknights adventure*

**Tide Callers' Guild**
Maritime organization of sailors, navigators, and weather-watchers. Provide shipping services, coastal rescue, and navigation expertise. Essential for Shattered Coast and maritime trade. *See: Organizations chapter*

**Tillus Merrion** (TIL-us MAIR-ee-on)
Human council member in Welton. Practical village leader handling administrative matters and community decisions. Concerned about wolf attacks threatening his community. *See: People of Northreach chapter, Wolves of Welton adventure*

**Tulgi Lutan** (TOOL-gee LOO-tan)
*Goliath name. Stress first syllable of each name.*
Goliath healer in Palebank Village. Herbalist and practical medicine provider. Treats mundane injuries and illnesses with natural remedies. Caring but gruff. *See: People of Northreach chapter*

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA}}

\page

## U

**Unmasked Parliament**
Governing council of Vharoxis. Operates without masks (unusual for Vharoxis culture), signaling transparency in official capacity. Manages city infrastructure and mediates disputes. Limited power—much of Vharoxis operates outside official channels. *See: Organizations chapter, Vharoxis chapter*

**Urgon Wenth** (UR-gon WENTH)
*Dwarf name. Both parts rhyme with "fur-gone" and "tenth"*
Dwarf blacksmith in Palebank Village. Provides weapon repair, metal goods, and smithing services. Traditional craftsman maintaining dwarven quality standards. Reliable and fair. *See: People of Northreach chapter*

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA}}

\page

## V

**Vaeltharyn** (VALE-thar-in)
*Elven name. Stress first syllable.*
Capital city of the Nullwood Expanse. Great elven metropolis grown into living trees. Center of memory preservation and silent culture. Known for vast libraries, whisper chambers, and living architecture. *See: Nullwood Expanse chapter*

**Verdant Marches, The** (VER-dent MAR-chez)
Fertile farmland region of central Aevoria. Breadbasket of the continent. Known for agriculture, seasonal festivals, and nature-aligned worship. Home to Solace Nexus ley-line port. *See: Regions chapter*

**Verdant Mother, The**
Nature deity of growth, seasons, and balance. Patron of farmers, druids, and those living in harmony with natural cycles. Worship involves seasonal festivals and offerings. *See: Gods and Religion chapter*

**Vharoxis** (vah-ROX-iss)
*Stress middle syllable: "vah-ROX-iss"*
Outlaw city on the southern coast. Known for mask culture, black market trade, and absence of traditional law. "What you can keep is yours." Operates on reputation, contracts, and personal power. Dangerous but full of opportunities unavailable elsewhere. *See: Regions chapter*

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote GLOSSARY OF AEVORIA}}

\page

## W

**Waystone Inn**
Headquarters of the Northwatch Wardens. Fortified inn serving as guild base, lodging, tavern, and community hub. Run by halfling chef Bordel Barleywind. Located centrally in Northreach territory. *See: Northwatch Wardens chapter*

**Welton**
Farming village southwest of Waystone Inn. Agricultural community experiencing mysterious wolf attacks in the Wolves of Welton adventure. Home to the Shepherd's Crook Inn. *See: Northreach chapter, Wolves of Welton adventure*

**Westly**
Shepherd in Welton whose farm is attacked by awakened wolves. Frightened but trying to protect his livelihood. Hires Northwatch Wardens to investigate. *See: Wolves of Welton adventure*

**Westly's Farm**
Sheep farm west of Welton. Site of initial wolf attacks that trigger the Wolves of Welton adventure. Remote location with vulnerable livestock. *See: Wolves of Welton adventure*

**Wild Sheep Chase, The**
Comic relief adventure involving polymorphing wizard Noke, his sheep-brother Finethir, and aggressive awakened sheep. Lighthearted tone but connects to campaign themes of destabilizing magic. *See: Wild Sheep Chase adventure*

**Willen Featherock**
Aarakocra scout and Northwatch Warden. Airborne reconnaissance specialist providing aerial perspective and scouting. Enthusiastic, helpful, sometimes fails to understand ground-based limitations. Based at Waystone Inn. *See: People of Northreach chapter*

**Wolves of Welton**
Adventure involving awakened wolves with developing intelligence attacking farms near Welton. First major indication of the Aeorian Echo phenomenon affecting wildlife. Moral complexity—wolves aren't evil, just hungry and confused. *See: Wolves of Welton adventure*

# THE FRONTIER BREATHES

### LANTERNS AT THE WAYSTONE  

#### Verse 1
There’s a lantern at the Waystone Inn
That never seems to fade.
Through winter storms and drifting snows,
Its golden light is laid.
Travelers say the hearth burns warm
No matter how winds roar—
And the road feels shorter somehow
When you’re walking toward its door.

#### Chorus
Lanterns at the Waystone,
Shining through the night.
Guiding weary footsteps
By their gentle, steady light.
Lanterns at the Waystone,
Soft against the cold—
A quiet place on a long, long road,
Where stories rest untold.

#### Verse 2
Some swear the air grows calmer there,
As if the world exhales.
Others say the shadows fall
In strangely peaceful trails.
But no one speaks of omens,
And no one asks for signs—
They simply take their comfort
In the warmth the inn provides.

#### Chorus
Lanterns at the Waystone,
Shining through the night.
Guiding weary footsteps
By their gentle, steady light.
Lanterns at the Waystone,
Soft against the cold—
A quiet place on a long, long road,
Where stories rest untold.

#### Bridge
Maybe it’s the timber,
Maybe it’s the stone—
Maybe it’s the feeling
Of never being quite alone.

#### Final Chorus
Lanterns at the Waystone,
Shining through the night.
Guiding weary footsteps
By their gentle, steady light.
Lanterns at the Waystone,
Soft against the cold—
A quiet place on a long, long road,
Where stories rest untold.

\column

### THE HUNTER WHO RETURNED ALONE  

#### Verse 1
They say the snows were higher then,
The winds a sharper blade.
The hunters marched at winter’s call
Through shadowed, frozen glade.
But only one came walking back,
Her bowstring stiff with frost—
And no one asked what met them there,
Or what the others lost.

#### Chorus
Oh the winter keeps its secrets,
And the pines, they never tell.
Some roads lead home in silence,
Some wanderings end in hell.
But the Hunter who returned alone
Still walks the northern stone—
And the wind that follows at her heels
Is colder than the bone.

#### Verse 2
She never speaks of what she saw,
Nor names the ones she led.
But when the moon is thin and pale,
Her eyes turn toward the dead.
The Wardens know her steady hand,
Her voice that does not shake—
But none can read the quiet grief
That winter will not break.

#### Chorus
Oh the winter keeps its secrets,
And the pines, they never tell.
Some roads lead home in silence,
Some wanderings end in hell.
But the Hunter who returned alone
Still walks the northern stone—
And the wind that follows at her heels
Is colder than the bone.

#### Bridge
Some say the storm remembers,
Some say the night does too—
But she just keeps on walking,
As all true hunters do.

#### Final Chorus
Oh the winter keeps its secrets,
And the pines, they never tell.
Some roads lead home in silence,
Some wanderings end in hell.
But the Hunter who returned alone
Still walks the northern stone—
And the wind that follows at her heels
Is colder than the bone.

---

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote THE FRONTIER BREATHES}}

\page

### THE WOMAN WITH TWO SHADOWS  

#### Verse 1
There’s a tale they tell in market towns
Of a woman quick and bright—
Who walks as if she listens
To footsteps out of sight.
They say she keeps her ledger clean,
Her smile warm and wide—
But some swear when the lanterns dim,
A second shadow walks beside.

#### Chorus
Oh the woman with two shadows,
She moves like shifting sand.
One rooted in the daylight,
One reaching for her hand.
No one knows her story,
No one speaks her name—
But the woman with two shadows
Walks faster than her shame.

#### Verse 2
She bargains fair with merchants,
She laughs with honest folk—
But travelers whisper softly
Of debts that never spoke.
And though she keeps her head down low,
Her eyes still scan the door—
As if she fears a knocking
From a life she knew before.

#### Chorus
Oh the woman with two shadows,
She moves like shifting sand.
One rooted in the daylight,
One reaching for her hand.
No one knows her story,
No one speaks her name—
But the woman with two shadows
Walks faster than her shame.

#### Bridge
Some say she fled the winter,
Some say she fled the knife—
But all agree her shadows
Have followed all her life.


#### Final Chorus
Oh the woman with two shadows,
She moves like shifting sand.
One rooted in the daylight,
One reaching for her hand.
No one knows her story,
No one speaks her name—
But the woman with two shadows
Walks faster than her shame.

---
\column
### THE SLEEPLESS SCHOLAR  

#### Verse 1
There’s a candle in the tower
That burns through every night.
A scholar keeps his vigil there
By thin and silver light.
He writes of winds that wander wrong,
Of stars that shift their place—
And though he speaks in gentle tones,
There’s worry in his face.

#### Chorus
Oh the sleepless scholar watches
While the northern shadows grow.
He listens to the quiet
For things he cannot show.
And though his words are measured,
And though his smile is mild—
The sleepless scholar knows too much
To ever sleep like a child.

#### Verse 2
Some say he dreams with open eyes,
Of frost beneath the stone—
Of something stirring far away
In places long unknown.
He never speaks of visions,
He never names the signs—
But he keeps his quill at ready
When the winter moon declines.

#### Chorus
Oh the sleepless scholar watches
While the northern shadows grow.
He listens to the quiet
For things he cannot show.
And though his words are measured,
And though his smile is mild—
The sleepless scholar knows too much
To ever sleep like a child.

#### Bridge
The Wardens trust his wisdom,
Though they do not know its cost—
For every night he studies
Is another morning lost.

#### Final Chorus
Oh the sleepless scholar watches
While the northern shadows grow.
He listens to the quiet
For things he cannot show.
And though his words are measured,
And though his smile is mild—
The sleepless scholar knows too much
To ever sleep like a child.

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote THE FRONTIER BREATHES}}

\page

### THE SHEPHERD WHO HEARD THE HILLS SPEAK  

#### Verse 1
They say he walks the Welton fields
Before the break of day,
Listening to the quiet earth
In his own peculiar way.
He knows the paths the rivers take,
The turns the foxes choose—
And he can read the winter wind
Like others read the news.

#### Chorus
Oh the hills speak softly
To the ones who walk alone.
Their whispers ride the morning frost,
Their secrets carved in stone.
And though he never tells them,
And though he never seeks—
The shepherd of the Welton fields
Once heard the hillside speak.

#### Verse 2
Some claim he knows the wolves by name,
And they know him in kind.
He walks the borders unafraid
With steady heart and mind.
But when the moon is hanging low
And shadows stretch and creep—
He pauses, as if listening
To something in the deep.

#### Chorus
Oh the hills speak softly
To the ones who walk alone.
Their whispers ride the morning frost,
Their secrets carved in stone.
And though he never tells them,
And though he never seeks—
The shepherd of the Welton fields
Once heard the hillside speak.

#### Bridge
A dream can be a warning,
A dream can be a guide—
But some dreams stay unspoken,
Kept quietly inside.

#### Final Chorus
Oh the hills speak softly
To the ones who walk alone.
Their whispers ride the morning frost,
Their secrets carved in stone.
And though he never tells them,
And though he never seeks—
The shepherd of the Welton fields
Once heard the hillside speak.

---
\column

### TRACKS IN THE SNOW THAT NEVER FADE  

#### Verse 1
There’s a tale the rangers whisper
When the winter nights grow long—
Of a man who walks the northern trails
With silence in his song.
They say he knows the forest well,
Each ridge and frozen glade—
But he avoids a certain hollow
Where old tracks never fade.

#### Chorus
Oh the snow remembers footsteps,
And the wind recalls the cries.
Some paths are marked by shadows,
Some truths by silent eyes.
And though he walks with steady stride,
His heart is heavy‑laid—
For he has seen the kind of tracks
That never truly fade.

#### Verse 2
He keeps his stories close at hand,
His memories even closer.
He speaks of wolves with reverence,
Of winter growing colder.
But when the fire burns low at night,
And talk begins to stray—
He stares into the embers
As if they pull him far away.

#### Chorus
Oh the snow remembers footsteps,
And the wind recalls the cries.
Some paths are marked by shadows,
Some truths by silent eyes.
And though he walks with steady stride,
His heart is heavy‑laid—
For he has seen the kind of tracks
That never truly fade.

#### Bridge
Some say he guards a secret,
Some say he guards a friend—
But all agree the northern trails
Will follow him to end.

#### Final Chorus
Oh the snow remembers footsteps,
And the wind recalls the cries.
Some paths are marked by shadows,
Some truths by silent eyes.
And though he walks with steady stride,
His heart is heavy‑laid—
For he has seen the kind of tracks
That never truly fade.

---

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote THE FRONTIER BREATHES}}

\page

### THE GIRL WHO FEARED THE MOONLIT PINES

#### Verse 1
She walks with steady footsteps
And her armor gleams like dawn—
But when the night wind stirs the pines,
Her courage feels withdrawn.
For somewhere in the shadows,
Where the silver moonlight spills,
She hears a distant memory
That time has never stilled.

#### Chorus
Oh the moonlit pines remember,
And the winter winds recall—
The cries that fade in darkness,
The names we never call.
And though she stands unshaken
When danger draws its lines—
Her heartbeat quickens softly
Near the moonlit, whispering pines.

#### Verse 2
She trains with blade and discipline,
Her stance both sharp and true—
But when the wolves begin to howl,
Her breath comes cold and few.
She hides it from her comrades,
She hides it from herself—
But fear can linger quietly
Like a book upon a shelf.

#### Chorus
Oh the moonlit pines remember,
And the winter winds recall—
The cries that fade in darkness,
The names we never call.
And though she stands unshaken
When danger draws its lines—
Her heartbeat quickens softly
Near the moonlit, whispering pines.

#### Bridge
Some wounds are carved in silence,
Some griefs are never named—
But still she walks the northern trails,
Determined, unashamed.

#### Final Chorus
Oh the moonlit pines remember,
And the winter winds recall—
The cries that fade in darkness,
The names we never call.
And though she stands unshaken
When danger draws its lines—
Her heartbeat quickens softly
Near the moonlit, whispering pines.

### THE SHEPHERD WHO HEARD TOO MUCH  


#### Verse 1

To hills both deep and wide.

Has left him pale and worn—

### TOMORROW’S TUNE  


#### Verse 1

In taverns warm and bright—

But sometimes in his singing,
A strange refrain appears—
A line that feels like memory
From days not yet near.

#### Chorus

In the corner of his mind—
A song that runs ahead of him,
A step beyond the time.
And though he laughs and shrugs it off,

There’s something oddly familiar
In the notes of tomorrow’s tune.

# Welcome to Northreach




Northreach is the kind of place that doesn’t announce itself with walls and banners — it reveals itself mile by mile. Wind combs through pine and scrub, the road narrows and widens like a breathing thing, and every settlement feels earned: a warm window in a wide, cold land.

The Wardens’ work begins where ordinary help ends. Their name passes from hearth to hearth in the same breath as practical advice: “Stay on the road,” “Don’t travel alone after dusk,” “If you’re in trouble, get word to the Waystone.” 

{{wide

![Northreach player map](https://i.imgur.com/GJBMEOh.jpg){{}}

}}

When winter bites early, when rumors travel faster than wagons, and when something in the dark makes even seasoned hunters hesitate, people look for the ones who will show up anyway—boots muddy, lamp lit, and questions asked only after everyone is safe.

{{note
This journal is your record of what you’ve seen and what you’ve chosen: the names you’ve learned, the promises you’ve made, and the trail of small facts that become a story. Keep it honest, keep it clear, and let it grow as Northreach grows familiar.
}}


![Wardens Logo](https://i.imgur.com/h0kcFqO_d.png){width:250px,border:"2px solid",border-radius:10px,float:"left",margin:"2px"}

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote WELCOME TO NORTHREACH}}

\page




---


# 1) Northreach Lore Primer (Common Knowledge)

Northreach is a frontier region—**wide roads, sparse settlements, and long stretches of wilderness** stitched together by stubborn persistence and the promise of the next warm hearth. Here, the horizon is big enough to make even confident travelers feel small: dark treelines crowd the road’s edge, weather turns on a whim, and the silence between wagon ruts can feel like it’s listening.

Life in Northreach runs on practical virtues. A sharp axe, a steady hand, and the habit of keeping your word matter more than titles. Folks remember who mends a broken fence without being asked, who shares a lantern when the fog rolls in, and who pays their tab before the dawn. Community isn’t a slogan out here—it’s a tool for survival, as vital as rope or tinder.

Trouble comes with the territory, and everyone knows it. Most dangers are ordinary: hunger, cold, and distance. Some are less easily named—strange tracks after fresh snow, animals that won’t spook, lights where there shouldn’t be any. Whatever the cause, Northreach respects anyone willing to step forward, take responsibility, and see a hard problem through to the end.


## 1.1 The Northwatch Wardens (The Guild)

The Northwatch Wardens are a contract-based guild headquartered at the **Waystone Inn**.

#### What most locals believe about Wardens:
- They handle problems that are too dangerous, too strange, or too urgent for town militias.
- They’re not nobles, not soldiers, and not priests—just professionals with a code.
- They can be hired, but they’re expected to protect innocents and keep their word.

#### Guild leadership:
- **Marshal Brenna Thorne** — the public face and final call on field matters.
- **Steward Mara Fenwick** — logistics, supplies, pay, and the contract board.
- **Lorewarden Elric Vael** — records, reports, and “what we know so far.”

## 1.2 Daily life on the frontier

#### Work and trade
- Most folk farm, herd, cut timber, trap, fish, or run small services for travelers.
- Coin is welcome, but **barter** is common away from trade hubs.

#### Law and order
- Settlements generally rely on councils, elders, or a small watch.
- Serious disputes tend to be settled by **community pressure** first, then fines, then exile.
- Outsiders who cause trouble are dealt with quickly—frontier towns can’t afford long grudges.

#### Hospitality and caution
- A warm meal and a bed can be had—if you’re respectful.
- People share warnings freely, but details are often colored by fear and superstition.

## 1.3 Travel in Northreach

#### Roads and routes
- Roads are real but imperfect: washouts, mud, and fallen trees are routine.
- Travel is slower in bad weather; caravans prefer predictable routes between settlements.

#### What travelers pack
- Oilskin cloak, spare socks, rope, a lantern, trail rations, and a waterskin.
- A small gift (tea, salt, needles) opens doors in hard places.

#### Common dangers
- Wolves and other predators
- Bandits and opportunists
- Sudden weather shifts
- “Old places” in the wilds that sensible folk avoid

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote 1) NORTHREACH LORE PRIMER (COMMON KNOWLEDGE)}}

\page

## 1.4 Magic (as everyday people understand it)
Northreach is not a place where magic is commonplace.
- Most residents have **heard of magic**.
- Fewer have **seen** it.
- Those who have tend to talk about it carefully—half in awe, half in fear.


## 1.5 Places of Northreach (Canonical)
Below are the places people in the region would recognize by name. (Some are familiar, some are “heard-of,” and some are local legend.)


### Waystone Inn (Center)

 - **What it is:** A well-known inn and the Wardens’ headquarters.
 - **What people say:** “If you can’t find help anywhere else, try Waystone.”
 - **What a visitor should know:** Neutral ground—start trouble there and you’ll be remembered.

### Welton (Southwest)

 - **What it is:** A farming and herding village.
 - **What people say:** “Good folk. Good bread. Keep your animals penned.”
 - **What a visitor should know:** Respect local customs; don’t mock superstitions.

### Westly’s Farm (West of Welton)
 - **What it is:** A well-known outlying farmstead.
 - **What people say:** “Hard work, hard land.”
 - **What a visitor should know:** Farms out here can be isolated—help is far away.

### Shepherd’s Crook Inn (In Welton)
 - **What it is:** Welton’s social heart: meals, gossip, and news.
 - **What people say:** “If you want the truth, buy a round.”
 - **What a visitor should know:** The innkeeper hears everything; behave accordingly.

\column

### Pinebrook (Southeast)
 - **What it is:** A trading village with regular traffic.
 - **What people say:** “If it’s for sale in the region, it passes through Pinebrook.”
 - **What a visitor should know:** Prices rise fast when rumors of danger spread.

### Palebank Village (Northeast coast)
 - **What it is:** A cold coastal settlement that survives on grit and cooperation.
 - **What people say:** “The sea provides—until it takes.”
 - **What a visitor should know:** Don’t underestimate cold; locals will quietly judge you for it.

### Temple of the Dragonknights (Northwest mountains)
 - **What it is:** A remote ruin in the mountains.
 - **What people say:** “A place built for heroes… and to bury what heroes couldn’t kill.”
 - **What a visitor should know:** Mountain travel turns deadly fast.

### Noke’s Tower (West of Waystone)
 - **What it is:** A wizard’s tower that’s become part warning, part campfire story.
 - **What people say:** “Stay on the road and don’t touch anything that glows.”
 - **What a visitor should know:** If you see lights where there shouldn’t be lights—leave.

## 1.6 Rumors (Unverified)

### Welton rumors
- Wolves have been seen closer to fences than usual.
- Someone swears they saw a gate left open with no prints nearby.
- A traveler mentioned “a missing spell-slinger,” but no one agrees on the details.
- Rare, whispered: “Some wolves understand words.”

### Palebank rumors
- A strange illness has people worried.

{{footnote 1) NORTHREACH LORE PRIMER (COMMON KNOWLEDGE)}}

## 1.7 People of the Wardens
